Ziyadat al-Thiqa and Its Fiqh Impact: The Dog-Sale Hadith
Analyzing the addition in the dog-selling hadith and its impact on juristic differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ziyadat al-thiqa to evaluate the addition in the dog-selling hadith and identify its fiqh consequence.

Core Idea
An addition by a trustworthy narrator can change a ruling, but its acceptance depends on weighing against other narrations.

This lesson examines a key example of how a single hadith variant (ziyadah) can lead to divergent fiqh rulings. The hadith on selling dogs was transmitted with and without an exception for trained hunting dogs. Understanding the Hanafi position on 'ziyadat al-thiqa' is crucial for deriving the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the variant text (ziyadah)
Locate the addition in the hadith: the exception for trained hunting dogs from the general prohibition on selling dogs.
The addition is narrated by Hammad and others.
2
Analyze the transmission: which narrators included/excluded the addition
Compare chains: Hammad and some others include the addition; many other narrators (e.g., Ma'qil ibn 'Ubayd Allah, Ibn Lahi'a, Abu Sufyan, 'Ata', Shurahbil) omit it.
The majority of narrators did not include the exception.
3
Apply the principle of ziyadat al-thiqa
In Hanafi usul, an addition from a trustworthy narrator (thiqa) is generally accepted if it does not contradict a more reliable source. Here, Ibn al-Turkumani argues the chain is good and the addition must be accepted.
The Hanafi school often accepts such additions, leading to the permissibility of selling trained dogs.
4
Evaluate the opposing argument
Opponents (Ibn Hibban, al-Bayhaqi) reject the addition because it is not found in most narrations, suggesting Hammad made a mistake. They argue that the authentic hadiths prohibit all dog sales.
This represents the Shafi'i position and the majority of hadith scholars.
5
Determine the fiqh outcome (thamarah)
The practical consequence: those who accept the addition permit selling a trained hunting dog only; those who reject it prohibit all dog sales.
This shows how a single textual variation can create a significant difference in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
محمد والهيثم بن جميل جميعهم رووه مرفوعاً، وفيه ذكر الزيادة. ورواه عبد الواحد بن غياث عن حماد موقوفاً، وفيه ذكر الزيادة. ورواه عبيد الله بن موسى بالشك عن حماد، وفيه ذكر الزيادة. ومع اتساع الخلاف في رواية حماد فقد خولف حماد في روايته للزيادة. فقد خالفه معقل بن عبيد الله وابن لهيعة كلاهما عن أبي الزبير، عن جابر بدون ذكر الزيادة. وللحديث طرق أخرى عن جابر بدون ذكر الزيادة: فقد رواه أبو سفيان وعطاء وشرحبيل ثلاثتهم عن جابر دون ذكر الزيادة، مما يدل على خطأ حماد في ذكرها إذ ليس من المعقول أن يغفل عنها الرواة في جميع الطبقات ويحفظها حماد. إلا أن بعض العلماء يعد هذه الزيادة زيادة ثقة يتعين قبولها، فقد قال ابن التركماني: «هذا إسناد جيد، فظهر أن الحديث صحيح، والاستثناء زيادة على أحاديث النهي عن ثمن الكلب فوجب قبولها». وقد ضعف ابن حبان هذه الزيادة فقال: «هذا الخبر بهذا اللفظ لا أصل له، ولا يجوز ثمن الكلب المعلم ولا غيره». وكذلك البيهقي فقال: «الأحاديث الصحاح عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في النهي عن ثمن الكلب خالية من هذا الاستثناء، وإنما الاستثناء في الأحاديث الصحاح في النهي عن الاقتناء ولعله شبه على من ذكر في حديث النهي عن ثمنه من هؤلاء الرواة الذين هم دون الصحابة والتابعين والله أعلم». أثر هذه الزيادة في اختلاف الفقهاء : حكم بيع الكلب المعلم اختلف الفقهاء في حكم بيع الكلب فقد ذهبت جماعة من أهل العلم إلى جواز بيع كلب الصيد دون غيره، روي هذا عن جابر بن عبد الله وأبي هريرة.
Third Chapter: Difference in Chain and Text. Muhammad and al-Haytham ibn Jamil all narrated it marfu', and in it the addition is mentioned. And 'Abd al-Wahid ibn Ghiyath narrated it from Hammad as mauquf, and in it the addition is mentioned. And 'Ubayd Allah ibn Musa narrated it with doubt from Hammad, and in it the addition is mentioned. And despite the extent of disagreement in Hammad's narration, Hammad was contradicted in his narration of the addition. Ma'qil ibn 'Ubayd Allah and Ibn Lahi'a both narrated from Abu al-Zubayr from Jabir without mentioning the addition. And there are other chains from Jabir without the addition: Abu Sufyan, 'Ata', and Shurahbil all narrated from Jabir without mentioning the addition, indicating Hammad's error in mentioning it, since it is inconceivable that all the narrators across all levels would neglect it while Hammad preserved it. However, some scholars consider this addition a trustworthy addition that must be accepted. Ibn al-Turkumani said: 'This is a good chain, so it appears the hadith is authentic, and the exception is an addition to the hadiths prohibiting the price of a dog, so it must be accepted.' Ibn Hibban weakened this addition, saying: 'This report in this wording has no basis, and the price of the trained dog or any other is not permissible.' Likewise, al-Bayhaqi said: 'The authentic hadiths from the Prophet, peace be upon him, prohibiting the price of a dog are free of this exception; the exception is only in the authentic hadiths prohibiting keeping dogs, and perhaps it was confused for those who mentioned it in the hadith prohibiting its price among these narrators who are below the Companions and Followers, and Allah knows best.' The effect of this addition on juristic differences: the ruling on selling the trained dog. The jurists differed on the ruling of selling dogs; a group of scholars went to the permissibility of selling a hunting dog only, and this is reported from Jabir ibn 'Abd Allah and Abu Hurayra.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith variant (ziyadah) regarding the sale of dogs. The author first presents the transmission history: several narrators, including Hammad, transmitted the hadith with an addition that excepts trained dogs from the prohibition. However, other reliable narrators transmitted the same hadith without this addition, leading to a dispute about its authenticity. The author then presents two opposing scholarly positions: Ibn al-Turkumani argues that the addition is a trustworthy addition (ziyadat thiqah) and must be accepted, whereas Ibn Hibban and al-Bayhaqi reject it, considering it a mistake by Hammad because the majority of narrators did not include it. Finally, the author shows the concrete fiqh consequence: those who accept the addition permit selling a trained hunting dog, while those who reject it prohibit all dog sales. This demonstrates how a single textual variation in a hadith can produce a significant difference in legal rulings.

Key Terms
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): إضافة لفظية من راوٍ ثقة ليست في رواية غيره، وهل تقبل مطلقا أم بشرط؟
الكلب المعلم (al-kalb al-mu'allam): الكلب المدرب على الصيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the concrete fiqh difference resulting from the acceptance or rejection of the addition in the hadith on selling dogs?
A) Those who accept the addition permit selling a trained hunting dog; those who reject it prohibit all dog sales.
B) Those who accept the addition prohibit all dog sales; those who reject it permit selling all dogs.
C) There is no difference; all scholars agree that selling dogs is prohibited.
D) The addition only affects the ruling on keeping dogs, not selling them.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance or rejection of a ziyadat al-thiqa can lead to opposing fiqh rulings, as demonstrated by the permissibility of selling trained dogs.

How a Hadith Increase (Ziyada) Changes the Ruling on Selling Dogs
Shows how a disputed increase in a hadith leads to divergent rulings on selling dogs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle regarding ziyada (addition in hadith) to explain the disagreement among madhhabs on the permissibility of selling dogs, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A single added phrase in a hadith can cause a major fiqh split—accepting it makes dogs saleable, rejecting it bans their sale.

This lesson explores a classic case where a textual variant in a hadith leads directly to a substantive legal disagreement. The Hanafi school relies on a version of the hadith that includes an additional phrase (ziyada) narrated by Hammad, permitting the sale of dogs under certain conditions. The majority of scholars, including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, adhere to the version without this addition, which they consider authentic, and thus prohibit the sale of all dogs. By studying this dispute, you will see how the usul principle of accepting or rejecting a ziyada determines the fiqh outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hadith versions
Locate in the source passage the hadith prohibiting the price of a dog. Note that the Hanafi version includes an addition (ziyada) narrated by Hammad, while the majority version does not.
The addition likely qualifies the prohibition to certain types of dogs.
2
Classify the textual variant
Determine whether the addition is considered a trustworthy ziyada from a reliable narrator or anomalous (shadh) according to each school's criteria.
Hanafis have conditions for accepting ziyada; Shafi'is consider it shadh if opposed by many.
3
State the Hanafi usul principle on ziyada
Recall that Hanafis accept a ziyada from a reliable narrator if it does not contradict stronger evidence. Here, the addition is preserved by Hammad and is not contradicted by an equally strong chain.
The hadith itself is ahad, so thubut is zanni.
4
Apply the principle to derive the Hanafi ruling
With the addition, the prohibition is restricted to dogs that are not permitted to keep. Dogs kept for hunting, herding, or farming are therefore excluded, making their sale permissible.
Abu Yusuf excludes biting dogs; the core Hanafi position permits trained and untrained dogs.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school rejects the addition as shadh and relies on the general prohibition. They also analogize dogs to pigs as najis animals, leading to a complete ban on selling dogs.
This creates a clear thamarah al-khilaf: validity of a dog sale contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن (۲) وعطاء، وزيد بن علي، والنخعي). والحجة لهم زيادة حماد السابقة. أما الإمام أبو حنيفة فيجوز عنده الكلب معلماً كان أو غير معلم في رواية الأصل). وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز بيع الكلب العقور؛ واستدلوا بأن الكلب منفعة يجوز بيعه. أما الإمام مالك فقد قال: «أكره ثمن الكلب الضاري وغير الضاري لنهي رسول الله عن ثمن الكلب». وقد وضح ابن عبد البر ذلك فقال: «وقد اختلف أصحاب مالك واختلفت الرواية عنده في ثمن الكلب الذي أبيح اتخاذه، فأجاز مرة ثمن الكلب الضاري، ومنع منه أخرى، ووجه إجازة بيع ما أبيح اتخاذه من الكلاب؛ لأن الحديث الذي ورد بالنهي عن ثمن الكلب، فمن نذر معه حلوان الكاهن ومهر البغي وهذا لا يباح شيء منه على أنه الكلب الذي لا يجوز اتخاذه والله أعلم؛ لأن من الكلاب ما أبيح اتخاذه، والانتفاع به، فذلك جائز بيعه». وعند الإمام مالك أن من قتل كلب صيد أو ماشية أو زرع فعليه قيمته. وذهب أكثر أهل العلم إلى أنه لا يجوز بيع الكلب سواء كان معلماً أو غير معلم، ولا ضمان على متلفه. روي هذا عن أبي هريرة، والحسن البصري، ومحمد بن سيرين، والحكم بن عتيبة، وحماد بن أبي سليمان، وربيعة الرأي، والأوزاعي، وابن أبي ليلى، وإليه ذهب الشافعي، وأحمد، وهو مذهب الظاهرية. واستدلوا بالحديث دون ذكر الزيادة وكأنها شاذة عندهم؛ لذا لم يعملوا بها، وقالوا أيضاً: بأن الكلب حيوان نجس لا يجوز بيعه كالخنزير.
Chapter Three / Difference in Chain and Text (2) And 'Ata', Zayd ibn 'Ali, and al-Nakha'i. Their proof is the addition of Hammad mentioned previously. As for Imam Abu Hanifa, he permits the sale of a dog whether trained or untrained according to the original narration. And from Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible to sell a biting dog; they argued that the dog's benefit permits its sale. As for Imam Malik, he said: 'I dislike the price of the predatory dog and the non-predatory dog due to the prohibition of the Messenger of Allah regarding the price of a dog.' And Ibn 'Abd al-Barr clarified that saying: 'The companions of Malik differed and the narration from him differed regarding the price of a dog whose keeping is permitted. He allowed the price of the predatory dog at one time and prohibited it at another. The justification for permitting the sale of dogs whose keeping is permitted is because the hadith that prohibits the price of a dog, along with the fee of the soothsayer and the dowry of the prostitute, nothing of that is permitted, and that applies to the dog whose keeping is not permitted, and Allah knows best, because among dogs there are those whose keeping and benefiting from them are permitted, so their sale is permissible.' And according to Imam Malik, whoever kills a dog used for hunting, livestock, or farming must pay its value. And the majority of scholars went to the opinion that it is not permissible to sell a dog, whether trained or untrained, and there is no liability on the one who destroys it. This is narrated from Abu Hurayrah, al-Hasan al-Basri, Muhammad ibn Sirin, al-Hakam ibn 'Utaybah, Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, Rabi'ah al-Ra'y, al-Awza'i, and Ibn Abi Layla. And al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and the Zahiri school went to this view. And they argued with the hadith without mentioning the addition, as if it was considered anomalous according to them, so they did not act upon it, and they also said that the dog is a najis animal and its sale is not permissible like the pig.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage from a study of differences in chains and texts presents the dispute over selling dogs. The key point is that the Hanafi school, relying on a version of the hadith that includes an addition (ziyada) narrated by Hammad, permits the sale of dogs. The addition likely made the prohibition specific to certain dogs or allowed benefit-based exceptions. In contrast, the majority of scholars, including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, rely on the version without this addition, which they consider sound, and also use analogy to the pig, which is najis and unsaleable. Imam Malik's position is nuanced: he dislikes it but in some transmissions permits it for dogs kept for hunting or farming, and imposes a penalty for killing such dogs. The passage illustrates how a difference in the transmission of a hadith (whether an extra phrase is present and considered reliable) leads directly to a difference in the fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An addition in the text of a hadith that is not present in other versions
شاذ (shadh): An anomalous narration that contradicts more reliable narrators

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key textual difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on selling dogs?
A) Hanafis consider dogs pure while Shafi'is consider them impure
B) Hanafis rely on a hadith with an additional phrase while Shafi'is rely on one without it
C) Hanafis allow only trained dogs while Shafi'is allow all dogs
D) There is no textual difference; the disagreement is on qiyas

Key Takeaway
The acceptance or rejection of a ziyada (addition) in a hadith is a fundamental usul difference that produces a clear thamarah al-khilaf on the permissibility of selling dogs.

Contested Increase: The Friday Ghusl Hadith Example
Illustrating how a narrator's addition is disputed by other reliable narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a contested ziyada, explain why it is disputed based on narrator reliability, and apply the Hanafi usuli principle regarding ziyada from a trustworthy narrator.

Core Idea
An addition to a hadith is not automatically accepted; its acceptance depends on the reliability of narrators who oppose or confirm it.

This passage presents a concrete example of how a narrated increase (ziyada) in a hadith text can be subject to dispute. The hadith about Friday ghusl is narrated with an extra phrase 'like ghusl of janabah' by 'Abd al-'Aziz, but other respected narrators like Malik and Sufyan did not include it. Understanding how scholars weigh such additions is crucial for sound hadith analysis and deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Locate the hadith and the contested phrase
Read the hadith: 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person like the ghusl of janabah.' The phrase 'like ghusl of janabah' is the ziyada under scrutiny.
This phrase is not present in all transmissions; it is an addition by 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad.
2
Identify the opposing narrators
The text states that 'Abd al-'Aziz was opposed by Malik and Sufyan. These narrators did not include the ziyada in their transmissions.
Malik and Sufyan are considered highly reliable; their omission creates a conflict.
3
Understand the methodological principle
The acceptance or rejection of a ziyada hinges on a comparison of narrator reliability. Hanafis generally accept a ziyada from a trustworthy narrator, but if more reliable narrators omit it, it may be considered shadh (anomalous) by other schools.
This principle directly impacts the ruling derived from the hadith.
4
Relate to usul al-fiqh
This example shows how textual variance leads to different legal conclusions. If the ziyada is accepted, the obligation is emphasized; if rejected, the ruling relies on other evidence.
This is a classic case of ikhtilaf arising from hadith transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد تكون الزيادة محتملة القبول والرد مثال ذلك ما روى عبد العزيز بن محمد عن صفوان بن سليم، عن عطاء بن يسار عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم كغسل الجنابة». هكذا رواه ابن حبان، عن أبي يعلى، عن محمد بن أبي بكر المقدمي وقد خولف عبد العزيز بن محمد في ذكر الزيادة خالفه مالك، وسفيان بن
And the increase may be subject to acceptance or rejection. An example of that is what 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad narrated from Safwan ibn Sulaym, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person like the ghusl of janabah.' Thus it was narrated by Ibn Hibban, from Abu Ya'la, from Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Muqaddami. And 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad was opposed in mentioning the increase; Malik and Sufyan ibn (the text ends).
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage provides a concrete example of how a narrated increase (ziyada) in a hadith text can be subject to dispute. The hadith about Friday ghusl is narrated by 'Abd al-'Aziz with the additional phrase 'like ghusl of janabah,' which would strengthen the obligation. However, other respected narrators like Malik and Sufyan did not include that phrase. The author offers this as an illustration of the principle that not all increases are automatically accepted; they may be considered shadh (anomalous) if reliable narrators oppose them. This is relevant to usul al-fiqh as it shows how the reliability of a chain and the presence of an additional phrase can affect the ruling derived from the hadith.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An addition to the hadith text that is not present in other transmissions
شاذ (shadh): A hadith narrated by a reliable narrator but contradicts a more reliable narrator; often defined as a rejected anomalous report.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who opposed 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad's addition in the Friday ghusl hadith?
A) Abu Hurairah
B) Ibn 'Umar
C) Malik and Sufyan
D) Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a ziyada (increase) in a hadith depends on a careful comparison of narrator reliability, not on a blanket rule of acceptance or rejection.

Ziyada in Hadith: The Friday Ghusl Dispute
Analyzing dispute over a hadith addition regarding Friday ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a ziyada in a hadith, apply the Hanafi principle for evaluating it, and derive the ruling consequence for the obligatory order in Friday ghusl.

Core Idea
An addition by a trustworthy narrator is accepted unless it contradicts a stronger transmission—then it becomes shadh and is left.

The Friday ghusl hadith contains a textual variant: some narrations include the phrase 'like ghusl of janabah' (كغسل الجنابة), while the majority omit it. This addition would imply that Friday ghusl must follow the same order as janabah ghusl—starting with the head. But is the addition accepted? Hanafi usul provides a clear method for weighing such a ziyada: it must be evaluated against the strength and number of opposing transmissions. In this lesson, we walk through the textual evidence, the list of narrators who omitted the addition, and the Hanafi reasoning that leads to a different ruling than the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Locate the ziyada
Find the addition 'كغسل الجنابة' in the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. It is the key textual element in dispute.
This addition is only present in the narration of 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad.
2
Identify the opposing narrations
List the narrators who transmitted the hadith without the addition (Malik, Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah, etc.). Count how many and assess their reliability.
The text lists 9 narrators who omitted the addition.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule for ziyada
Hanafis accept a ziyada from a trustworthy narrator unless it contradicts a stronger (more numerous or more reliable) narration. Here, the addition contradicts many trustworthy narrators, so it may be considered shadh.
This is a case of legitimate ikhtilaf; not all schools apply this preference.
4
Derive the ruling consequence
If the addition is accepted, Friday ghusl requires starting with the head (like janabah). If rejected, no specific order is required. State which ruling the Hanafi school adopts and why.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the obligatory order of washing.

Source Text

الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن (۲) روي هذا عن أبي هريرة )، والحسن البصري (٢)، ومحمد بن سيرين، والحكم بن عتيبة)، وحماد بن أبي سليمان)، وربيعة الرأي)، والأوزاعي)، وابن أبي ليلى). (۹) (19) وإليه ذهب الشافعي (9) ، وأحمد (۱) ، وهو مذهب الظاهرية(١١). واستدلوا بالحديث دون ذكر الزيادة وكأنها شاذة عندهم؛ لذا لم يعملوا بها، وقالوا أيضاً : بأن الكلب حيوان نجس لا يجوز بيعه كالخنزير. وقد تكون الزيادة محتملة القبول والرد مثال ذلك ما روى عبد العزيز بن مُحَمَّد (۱۲) عن صفوان بن سليم، عن عطاء بن يسار عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال: قال رسول الله : غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم كغسل الجنابة». هكذا رواه ابن حبان (۱٥)، عن أبي يعلى ، عن محمد بن أبي بكر المُقَدَّمي وقد خولف عبد العزيز بن محمد في ذكر الزيادة خالفه (مالك(۱۸)، وسفيان بن عيينة ()، وأبو علقمة الفروي () ، وأسامة بن زيد (۳) ، وعبد الرَّحمن بن زيد، وبكر بن (۲)، وائل)، والفضيل بن عياض (٦) ، وعبد الرَّحْمن بن إسحاق (۲)، فرووه عن صفوان بن (1)، عن عطاء بن يسار، عن أبي سعيد الخدري دون ذكر الزيادة " كغسل سلیم الجنابة". وللحديث شاهد من حديث أبي هريرة قال ابن حزم في المحلى (۱): وكل غسل ذكرنا فللمرء أن يبدأ به من رجليه أو من أي أعضائه شاء، حاشا غسل الجمعة والجنابة، فلا يجزئ فيهما إلا البداءة بغسل الرأس أولاً ثم الجسد، فإن انغمس في ماء فعليه أن ينوي البداءة برأسه ثم بجسده ولا بد». واستدل بقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: حق الله على كل مسلم أن يغتسل في كل سبعة أيام (٨٧٩) و ٦/٢ (٨٩٥)، وأبو داود (٣٤١)، والنسائي ۹۳/۳ وفي الكبرى، له (١٦٦٨)، وأبو عوانة ٤٦/٣ ، وابن خزيمة (١٧٤٢)، والطحاوي في شرح المعاني ،١١٦/١، وابن حبان (١٢٢٨) ط الرسالة والبيهقي في الكبرى ۲۹٤/١٨ و ۱۸۸/۳، والبغوي (۳۳۱). Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. (2) This was narrated by Abu Hurairah, al-Hasan al-Basri, Muhammad ibn Sirin, al-Hakam ibn Utaybah, Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, Rabi'ah al-Ra'y, al-Awza'i, and Ibn Abi Layla. (9) (19) Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad agreed with it, and it is the madhhab of the Zahiris. They adduced the hadith without mentioning the addition, as if it were shadh in their view; therefore they did not act upon it. They also said that the dog is a najis animal, its sale is not permissible like the pig. The addition may be subject to acceptance and rejection. An example of that is what 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad narrated from Safwan ibn Sulaym, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory for every adult male, like the ghusl of janabah.' Thus narrated by Ibn Hibban from Abu Ya'la, from Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Muqaddami. 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad was opposed in mentioning the addition; opposed by Malik, Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah, Abu 'Alqamah al-Farwi, Usamah ibn Zayd, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd, Bakr ibn Wa'il, al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad, and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ishaq. They narrated from Safwan ibn Sulaym, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri without mentioning the addition 'like the ghusl of janabah.' The hadith has a witness from the hadith of Abu Hurairah. Ibn Hazm said in al-Muhalla: 'Every ghusl we have mentioned, a person may start with his feet or any of his limbs he wishes, except Friday ghusl and janabah ghusl, for which it is not valid except to begin with washing the head first, then the body. If he immerses in water, he must intend starting with his head then his body, inevitably.' And he adduced the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'It is the right of Allah upon every Muslim to bathe every seven days...' (followed by references in footnotes).
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of how differences in hadith transmission (sanad and matn) lead to differing fiqh rulings. The author presents a dispute about the addition (ziyada) 'like ghusl of janabah' in the hadith on Friday ghusl. Some scholars accepted the addition and considered the obligation of Friday ghusl to be exactly like janabah ghusl, implying specific rulings like the order of washing. Others considered the addition shadh (irregular) and did not act upon it. The passage lists the narrators who omitted the addition, including Malik and Sufyan, indicating that the addition was not universally accepted. The author then quotes Ibn Hazm, who explicitly derived from the hadith (likely the version with the addition) that for Friday ghusl and janabah ghusl, one must start with the head. This shows the practical effect of accepting or rejecting a hadith addition. The passage also includes extensive references to hadith collections, demonstrating the scholarly method of citing sources. For a Hanafi student, this illustrates that not all narrations carry equal weight; the reliability of narrators and the consistency of transmission affect which version is adopted, and consequently the ruling derived.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An addition in the text of a hadith not found in other narrations.
شاذ (shādh): A narration that is inherently acceptable but conflicts with a stronger narration; considered irregular and left out.
شاهد (shāhid): A supporting hadith that corroborates the meaning, though not necessarily from the same companion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did some scholars (like those listed) not act upon the addition 'كغسل الجنابة' in the Friday ghusl hadith?
A) Because they considered the hadith weak overall.
B) Because the addition was narrated by a single narrator and contradicted by many trustworthy narrators, making it shadh.
C) Because they believed Friday ghusl is not obligatory.
D) Because the addition was only found in the narration of Ibn Hibban, who is unreliable.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance or rejection of a hadith addition (ziyada) depends on the strength of its transmission relative to other narrations, directly affecting the derived fiqh ruling.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
How Chain Variation Affects Hadith Text: Bilal's Adhan
Illustrating how narrator additions/omissions cause textual differences in hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how differences in chain (sanad) lead to textual differences (matn) and apply the Hanafi method of tarjih/jam' to reconcile such variations.

Core Idea
A narrator may add or omit a phrase; many chains for Bilal's adhan show the core ruling is consistent despite wording variations.

This passage demonstrates a key principle in Hanafi usul: when a hadith is transmitted through multiple chains with slight wording differences, the core meaning remains authoritative. Using the example of Bilal's adhan, the author shows how narrator additions or omissions create textual variation without undermining the ruling. Understanding this helps scholars resolve apparent contradictions and identify the most reliable transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples
The passage begins with an example about wudu order (head before body) using a Quranic verse to establish that the Prophet's actions are revelation. Then it introduces the main example: Bilal's adhan hadith. Focus on the adhan example.
The wudu example serves to reinforce the authority of the Prophet's actions.
2
Extract the core hadith wording
From the chains, the core wording is: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded Bilal to make the adhan with tathwib (shafa') and the iqama with witr (witr).' Note the key terms: tathwib (repeating) and witr (single).
Tathwib is the act of repeating the phrases twice; witr means once.
3
Analyze the chain variations
The author lists numerous chains (e.g., from Ayyub, Shu'ba, Wuhayb, etc.). Some narrators include the word 'tathwib' explicitly; others may omit it or use different phrasing. The variations are minor and do not change the essential command.
List of chains is extensive; the point is multiplicity, not each individual chain.
4
Apply Hanafi usul principles
Hanafi methodology resolves such variations by preferring stronger chains (tarjih) or harmonizing (jam') the wordings. Since the chains are numerous and include reliable narrators, the hadith is considered authentic (sahih) and the variation does not affect the ruling.
The Quranic verse cited (Najm 3-4) supports that the Prophet's speech is revelation, so any authentic transmission is binding.
5
Conclude on the significance
This example illustrates that chain variation does not automatically weaken a hadith; it can actually strengthen it through tawatur (mass transmission) if the variations are consistent in meaning. Hanafi jurists use this principle to confirm rulings and dismiss claims of contradiction.
This is a standard usul al-hadith tool used in fiqh derivation.

Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. '...day, he washes his head and body.' And his saying: 'Start with what Allah started with' (2), and he (peace be upon him) started with the head before the body. And Allah said: 'Nor does he speak from [his own] inclination; it is only a revelation revealed' (3). So it is established that what the Messenger of Allah started with in his speech is from revelation that came to him from Allah Almighty, so Allah is the One who started with what the Messenger of Allah started with. And the narrator may differ in an addition, mentioning it once and omitting it another time. An example of that is what Ayyub narrated from Abu Qilaba from Anas with the wording: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded Bilal to make the adhan with tathwib and the iqama with witr.' And from this chain it was recorded by Abu Awana... via Simak ibn Atiyya, and al-Tahawi via Amr al-Jazari, and Abu Awana, and Ibn Hibban via Shu'ba, and Abu Dawud, and Abu Ya'la, and Abu via Kharaja, and Awana from Wuhayb, and al-Daraqutni... (then lists of chains continue).
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on how differences in the chain of transmission (sanad) and the text (matn) cause legal differences among scholars. The author first gives an earlier example regarding wudu: the Prophet started washing his head before his body, and the command 'Start with what Allah started with' indicates that order is important. The Qur'anic verse proves that the Prophet's actions are based on revelation. Then the author states that a narrator may sometimes add a phrase and sometimes omit it, leading to textual variation. The main example is the hadith about Bilal being ordered to make the adhan with tathwib (repeating the call twice) and the iqama with witr (once). The author then lists numerous chains of transmission for this hadith, showing that even though the basic meaning is the same, some narrators include the word 'tathwib' while others do not, or vary the wording. This illustrates how differences in sanad can lead to differences in matn, and how scholars must reconcile these variations. The list of chains includes many narrators like Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani, Abu Qilaba, Simak, Shu'ba, Wuhayb, etc., all transmitting from Anas. The author is demonstrating that despite the many chains, the core text remains consistent, but minor additions or omissions occur. This is a key principle in usul al-fiqh: when multiple chains have variations, the most reliable version is taken, or the differences are resolved by considering the strength of the narrators and the context.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting a hadith from the Prophet to the compiler.
متن (matn): The text or content of the hadith, containing the actual words of the Prophet.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement or variation in the transmission (sanad) or wording (matn) of a hadith.
تثويب (tathwib): Repeating the adhan phrases twice (shafa'), as opposed to once (witir). In this hadith, the Prophet commanded Bilal to make adhan with tathwib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the variation in chains for Bilal's adhan hadith illustrate about Hanafi usul?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot be used.
B) The core meaning is consistent despite wording differences, and the hadith remains authentic.
C) The adhan ruling varies by chain.
D) The iqama should be said with tathwib.

Key Takeaway
Chain variation leads to textual differences, but in Hanafi usul, such variations are resolved through tarjih or jam', and the authentic hadith remains valid for deriving rulings.

Assessing Narrator Additions: The 'Except the Iqama' Case
Textual analysis of multiple chains for the adhan hadith focusing on the disputed addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ziyadat al-thiqa to evaluate whether a narrator's addition to a hadith is accepted as part of the prophetic text.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's addition to a hadith is accepted unless proven an interpolation; multiple corroborating chains strengthen acceptance.

This passage presents a detailed case study of how Hanafi usul handles conflicting transmissions of a hadith. At issue is whether the phrase 'except the iqama' (indicating the iqama is said once) is from the Prophet or an explanatory comment by the narrator Ayyub. By tracing numerous chains, the author demonstrates the Hanafi methodology for resolving such textual discrepancies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed element
Pinpoint the exact phrase in the hadith that is contested: 'except the iqama'. This addition changes the fiqh ruling on how many times the iqama is recited.
The disputed addition is a phrase, not the entire matn.
2
Survey the chains with the addition
Note the many narrators—Ma'mar, Sammak, Isma'il ibn 'Ulayya, and others—who transmitted the addition through Ayyub. This multiplicity is evidence of its authenticity.
List the narrators mentioned in the passage.
3
Analyze the objection
Some scholars (Ibn Manda, Abu Muhammad al-Asili) claim that the addition is Ayyub's own commentary, not the Prophet's words. Examine the basis: a version where Ayyub is reported to have said it separately.
The objection relies on a variant transmission.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule of ziyadat al-thiqa
The Hanafi usul principle accepts an addition by a trustworthy narrator as part of the hadith unless there is clear evidence of interpolation. Here, the addition is by Ayyub (a thiqa) and is corroborated by multiple chains.
Contrast with the opposing view that requires stronger proof for acceptance.
5
Evaluate supporting evidence
The passage also notes supporting evidence from the hadiths of Ibn Umar and Ibn Zaid, which further strengthen the case for accepting the addition.
These shawahid provide external corroboration.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of the chains of transmission for a hadith regarding the adhan (call to prayer) and iqama. The author is surveying the many paths through which the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (رضي الله عنه) has been narrated, focusing on the version that includes the phrase 'except the iqama'. The passage begins by listing a group of narrators (Sammak, 'Amr, Shu'ba, etc.) who all transmitted through Ayyub from Abi Qilaba from Anas. It then mentions a follow-up narration by Khalid al-Hadha', and provides an extensive list of additional chains traced through various hadith compilers like al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, etc. The key point of scholarly dispute is whether the addition 'except the iqama' (i.e., that the iqama is said once, not twice like the adhan) is part of the prophetic hadith or an explanatory comment by the narrator Ayyub. The passage notes that Ibn Manda and Abu Muhammad al-Asili claimed it was an insertion by Ayyub, but the author (likely quoting Ibn Hajar) argues that the original narration from Ayyub includes it, and that the default is to consider such additions as part of the hadith unless proven otherwise. The passage also provides supporting evidence from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar and 'Abdullah ibn Zaid.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators through which a hadith is transmitted.
متن (matn): The text of the hadith, whose wording may vary across different chains.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): An addition to a hadith made by a trustworthy narrator that is not found in other versions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a trustworthy narrator's addition (ziyadat al-thiqa) to a hadith is accepted unless clear evidence shows it is an interpolation.

How a Hadith Addition Creates a Fiqh Dispute
Hadith variant analysis leading to fiqh ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that an addition from a reliable narrator in a hadith is part of the sunnah, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf in the iqamah dispute.

Core Idea
An addition by a trustworthy narrator is accepted as part of the sunnah unless stronger evidence contradicts it.

This passage examines how a single additional phrase in a hadith—'except the iqamah'—narrated by Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani has profound effects on the fiqh ruling of the iqamah. The Hanafi school accepts this addition as prophetic, while other schools treat it as a narrator insertion. Understanding why this addition is accepted or rejected requires a firm grasp of the usul principle governing ziyadat al-thiqah (additions by reliable narrators) and the concept of mutaba'at (follow-up witnesses).

Guided Path
1
Identify the addition and its narrator chain
Locate the hadith addition 'except the iqamah' and trace the chain: Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani heard it from Abu Qilaba from Anas, and it was corroborated by Ma'mar, Simak, and Isma'il ibn 'Ulayya. Also note the chains of Sulayman al-Taymi and Qatada who narrated the same hadith without the addition.
The addition is 'qad qamat al-salah' twice; the debate is whether this was originally part of the Prophet's sunnah or inserted by Ayyub.
2
Apply the Hanafi usul principle on accepting additions
Recall the principle: 'ما كان في الخبر فهو منه حتى يقوم دليل على خلافه' – whatever is in the report is part of it unless evidence shows otherwise. Since Ayyub is reliable and his version is corroborated, the addition is accepted as part of the sunnah. This differs from some scholars who considered it an insertion by Ayyub.
The opposing view claims that because Khalid al-Hadhdha' (also from Abu Qilaba) did not mention the addition, Ayyub's version may be suspect. But the Hanafi response is that Khalid's omission does not prove the addition is false; it only shows he did not narrate it.
3
See the fiqh consequence: three madhhabs
The addition leads to three distinct positions: (1) iqamah like adhan + 'qad qamat al-salah' twice (Hanafi, many Companions), (2) iqamah with fewer takbirs, (3) iqamah with different phrasing. The Hanafi position is directly supported by the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd which includes the full text of the iqamah exactly as practiced.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual wording and number of repetitions in the iqamah, which affects the daily practice of millions.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is strengthened by multiple corroborating chains (mutaba'at) and the explicit text. The opposing view relies on a strict interpretation that rejects narrator additions unless widespread (tawatur). The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position that includes the addition.
Imam Abu Hanifa and his students preferred this view, and later Hanafi works like al-Hidayah adopt it as the relied-upon position.

Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. And Sulayman al-Taymi [1] complete follow-up, and Qatada [2] lower follow-up, except that Ayyub narrated the hadith with the previous chain and text and added in it 'except the iqamah' [3], and it was narrated from him by each of Ma'mar [4], Simak [5], and Isma'il ibn 'Ulayya [6]. And it has corroborative evidence from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar [7] and 'Abdullah ibn Zayd [8]... [Hadith analysis details]... Effect of this addition on the difference among jurists: Manner of the iqamah. The jurists differed on the iqamah according to three schools: The first school: holds that the iqamah is like the adhan except that it has the addition 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. This was held by some Companions including 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, Thawban, 'Abdullah ibn Zayd al-Ansari, Salama ibn al-Akwa', and it is a narration from Bilal and Abu Mahdhura. Also held by Abu al-'Aliya, al-Nakha'i, Mujahid, Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, and it is the school of the Zaydiyya. They adduced the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd... [full hadith].
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a case study in usul al-fiqh, demonstrating how a difference in the text of a hadith (the addition of 'except the iqamah' by Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani) leads to substantive disagreement among jurists regarding the wording of the iqamah. The author first traces the chains of transmission, noting that Ayyub added the phrase 'except the iqamah' to the standard adhan hadith, while others like Khalid al-Hadhdha' did not. The author then shows the fiqh consequence: three madhhabs emerge on the iqamah. The first madhhab, which includes Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that the iqamah is identical to the adhan in wording and number, except that after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' one says 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. This is supported by the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd, which explicitly includes the iqamah with that phrasing. The other two madhhabs (not fully detailed in this window) presumably differ on the number of repetitions or the inclusion of certain phrases. The Hanafi position is thus grounded in the narrated text, and the addition is considered part of the sunnah.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An additional phrase in a hadith that may affect the ruling derived from it.
متابعة (mutāba‘ah): A follow-up narration that corroborates the main chain; a 'complete follow-up' (mutaba'ah tammah) means another companion or student narrated it, a 'lower follow-up' (mutaba'ah nazilah) means from a later narrator.
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): The second call to prayer recited immediately before the obligatory prayer begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It should be rejected unless it is mutawatir

C) It should be accepted only if the majority of narrators agree
D) It should be treated as a narrator mistake because it contradicts the more famous version

Key Takeaway
A reliable narrator's addition to a hadith is accepted as part of the sunnah unless stronger evidence proves it is an insertion; this principle leads to the Hanafi ruling on the iqamah.

Dispute on the Wording of Iqamah: How Hadith Variations Cause Fiqh Differences
Comparison of three madhhab positions on Iqamah wording using hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key hadith variations regarding the wording of the Iqamah and explain how the Hanafi school uses the principle of naskh (abrogation) to prioritize the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah over the hadith of Bilal.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that the Iqamah repeats its phrases because a later hadith (Abu Mahdhurah) abrogates the earlier practice of Bilal.

Have you ever noticed that the Iqamah (second call to prayer) varies between madhhabs? This lesson explores why. The passage you will study compares three schools on whether the phrases in the Iqamah are repeated or said once. The differences stem from variations in hadith texts (ziyada) and the principle of abrogation (naskh). By examining the evidence, you will understand how the Hanafi school derives its position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three schools and their positions on Iqamah wording
The passage presents three madhhabs: Hanafi (first school), Maliki/old Shafi'i (second school), and a third view from some Companions. List the exact wording repetition for each (e.g., Hanafi: like Adhan but with 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice).
This step helps you map the ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the hadith evidence cited for each school
The Hanafis cite the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd (the dream hadith) and the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah. The Malikis cite the hadith of Anas about Bilal. The third view cites actions of Companions. Identify which hadith each school uses.
Pay attention to the chain and wording differences.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: how do they use ziyada and naskh?
The Hanafis argue that the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, which mentions 19 phrases for Adhan and 17 for Iqamah, abrogates the earlier hadith of Bilal (which only mentions Adhan). The hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd provides the detailed wording. Trace the logic of abrogation.
In Hanafi usul, a later hadith can abrogate an earlier one if the chain is authentic.
4
Evaluate the opposing evidence and the Hanafi response
The second school uses the hadith of Anas: 'Bilal was ordered to make the Adhan odd and the Iqamah even.' The Hanafis respond that this can be interpreted differently or that the practice was later changed. Note the response from the passage.
The response is implied: the detailed hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd is more comprehensive.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis repeat phrases in the Iqamah (e.g., 'Allahu akbar' four times, 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice), while Malikis say each phrase once. State the difference clearly.
This shows how a seemingly small hadith variation affects daily worship.

Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. The effect of this addition on the difference of jurists: the manner of the Iqamah. The jurists differed on how the Iqamah is, into three schools: The first school holds that the Iqamah is like the Adhan except that it has the addition of 'Qad qamat al-salah' twice. This is the view of some Companions including Ali ibn Abi Talib, Thawban, Abdullah ibn Zayd al-Ansari, Salamah ibn al-Akwa', and it is a narration from Bilal and Abu Mahdhurah. Also holding this view are Abu al-Aliyah, al-Nakha'i, Mujahid, Abu Hanifah, al-Thawri, Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, and it is the Zaydi school. They adduce the hadith of Abu Abdullah ibn Zayd who said: My father Abdullah ibn Zayd told me: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered the bell to be struck to gather the people for prayer, while I was asleep a man carrying a bell in his hand circled around me. I said to him: O servant of Allah, will you sell the bell? He said: What will you do with it? I said: We will summon to prayer with it. He said: Shall I guide you to something better than that? I said: Yes. He said: Say: Allahu akbar Allahu akbar Allahu akbar Allahu akbar, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasul Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasul Allah, Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah, Hayya 'ala al-falah, Allahu akbar Allahu akbar, La ilaha illa Allah. He said: Then he stepped back a little and said: Then when you establish the prayer, say: Allahu akbar Allahu akbar, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasul Allah, Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah, Qad qamat al-salah, Qad qamat al-salah, Allahu akbar Allahu akbar, La ilaha illa Allah... the hadith. The wording is from Ibn al-Jarud. (And the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah: that the Prophet taught him the Adhan as nineteen phrases and the Iqamah as seventeen phrases, and they hold that the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah abrogates the hadith of Bilal.) The second school holds that the phrases of the Iqamah are single, and his saying 'Qad qamat al-salah' is also once. This is the school of al-Layth ibn Sa'd, Malik, and al-Mawardi said: al-Shafi'i held it in his old opinion. They adduce the hadith of Anas who said: 'Bilal was ordered to make the Adhan odd and the Iqamah even.' The third school says: the wording of the Iqamah is single except for his saying 'Qad qamat al-salah' for he says it twice. This is narrated from the action of some Companions including Umar, Abdullah ibn Umar, Anas, and it is a narration from Bilal and Abu Mahdhurah - may Allah be pleased with them - and it is the view of 'Urwah ibn al-Zubayr, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, and 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a comparative fiqh analysis of the wording of the Iqamah (the second call to prayer). The author presents three schools of thought on how many times each phrase is repeated, based on different hadith texts. 

**First School (Hanafi, Zaydi, and others):** The Iqamah is like the Adhan but with 'Qad qamat al-salah' added twice. Evidence includes the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd (the dream hadith) and the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah which has 19 phrases for Adhan and 17 for Iqamah. They consider the Abu Mahdhurah hadith abrogating Bilal's practice.

**Second School (Maliki, old Shafi'i):** The Iqamah phrases are single (i.e., each phrase once), including 'Qad qamat al-salah'. They rely on the hadith of Anas that Bilal was ordered to make the Adhan witr (odd, i.e., twos) and the Iqamah witr (even, i.e., ones).

**Third School (some Companions and early scholars):** The Iqamah is single except 'Qad qamat al-salah' is said twice. This is attributed to Umar, Ibn Umar, Anas, and others.

The discussion exemplifies how variations in hadith chains and texts (ziyada, naskh) led to differing fiqh positions. The Hanafi position is based on the more detailed hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd and the apparent abrogation of earlier practice by Abu Mahdhurah's teaching.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqāma): The second call to prayer immediately before the congregation stands for prayer, consisting of specific phrases.
الأذان (al-adhān): The first call to prayer, announced to notify the time of prayer.
زيادة (ziyāda): An addition in the text of a hadith that is not present in another narration.
ناسخ (nāsikh): Abrogating; a later revelation or hadith that supersedes an earlier one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith of Anas that Bilal made the Iqamah even.
B) The hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd and the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah.
C) The practice of the people of Medina.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Differences in hadith texts (ziyada) and the principle of naskh (abrogation) are key usul tools that lead to valid fiqh differences, as seen in the wording of the Iqamah.

Rejecting Additions in Hadith: The Rule of Shiddat al-Fardiyya
States the principle for rejecting unusual additions in hadith and gives a specific example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of rejecting unusual additions (ziyada) in hadith due to extreme singularity and identify the criteria for their rejection.

Core Idea
An addition in a hadith that is singular and disputed is rejected—consistency with reliable narrations is paramount.

In this lesson, we examine a key rule of Hanafi hadith criticism: when an addition to a hadith is reported through a weak singular chain and conflicts with the widely transmitted version, it is rejected. We will analyze the example of the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr regarding hand placement in prayer, where the phrase 'on his chest' is not accepted due to its extreme singularity.

Guided Path
1
State the Rule
Identify the principle: an addition (ziyada) is rejected when it is disputed and extremely singular (shadid al-fardiyya).
2
Examine the Example
Look at the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr: the core hadith about placing right hand on left is well-known, but the addition 'on his chest' comes only through weak chains.
The addition is from Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il, a narrator with issues.
3
Analyze the Chains
The text mentions that the standard version is transmitted by many chains, whereas the addition is only through a few narrators like 'Asim ibn Kulayb and his father.
This creates shiddat al-fardiyya.
4
Apply the Rule
Because the addition is singular and disputed, it is rejected as unreliable. Hanafis do not use it as evidence.

وَقَدْ تُرَدُّ الزيادة للاختلاف فيها وشدة فرديتها، مثال ذلك حديث مؤمل بن إسماعيل، عن سفيان، عن عاصم بن كليب عن أبيه عن وائل بن حجر، قال صليت مع رسول الله هو وضع يده اليمنى على يده اليسرى على صدره. فقد ورد حديث وائل بن حجر وفيه وضع اليمين على الشمال من طرق عن بعض أهل بيت عبد الجبار، وأم عبد الجبار ، وعلقمة بن وائل (١٤)، وعبد الجبار بن
And the addition is rejected due to the disagreement about it and its extreme singularity; an example of that is the hadith of Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il, from Sufyan, from 'Asim ibn Kulayb, from his father, from Wail ibn Hujr, who said: I prayed with the Messenger of Allah, and he placed his right hand on his left hand on his chest. So the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr has been narrated containing placing the right on the left from multiple chains through some of the family of 'Abd al-Jabbar, and Umm 'Abd al-Jabbar, and 'Alqama ibn Wail, and 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn...
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage presents a rule in hadith criticism: an addition (ziyada) in a hadith that is not widely transmitted and is disputed among scholars is rejected (maradd). The example given is a hadith from Wail ibn Hujr that includes the phrase 'placed his right hand on his left on his chest'—an addition to the standard version. The text notes that the main hadith (about placing right on left, but not specifying 'on the chest') is narrated through many chains, but this specific addition only comes through a few weak or family chains, making it unreliable. The principle is used by Hanafi scholars to dismiss weak additions that contradict the well-known version. The example is incomplete on this page, but the rule is clear: the addition is rejected because of its extreme singularity (shiddat fardiyyatiha) and disagreement.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An extra phrase or action added to a hadith that is not found in the majority of narrations.
فردية (fardiyya): Singularity or aloneness; the quality of a hadith being narrated only by one person or a very small group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An addition in a hadith that is extremely singular and disputed is rejected; Hanafis prioritize widely transmitted versions.

Rejecting an Addition Due to Idtirab: The Case of Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il
Analyzing the addition 'ala sadrihi' in the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr and its weakness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an addition by a narrator is rejected due to idtirab and apply the Hanafi criterion for ziyadat al-thiqa to evaluate hadith evidence.

Core Idea
An addition from a trustworthy narrator is rejected if he is inconsistent in his transmission.

This passage uses a real hadith case to demonstrate that not every addition by a so-called trustworthy narrator is automatically accepted. Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il added the phrase 'on his chest' to the hadith of hand placement, but his inconsistency in narrating it causes his addition to be rejected. Understanding this principle sharpens your ability to weigh hadith evidence for fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main hadith and the addition
The hadith narrates how the Prophet placed his right hand on his left during prayer. The addition in question is the phrase 'on his chest' (على صدره).
2
Examine the narrator Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il
He is a hafiz but known for many errors; he buried his books and narrated from memory, causing doubts about his reliability.
See the biographical details in the footnotes.
3
Detect the idtirab (inconsistency)
Mu'ammal narrated the hadith in three different versions: 'on his chest', 'at his chest', and without any location. This inconsistency is idtirab.
4
Apply the principle: rejection of ziyada due to idtirab
In Hanafi usul, an addition from a narrator is accepted only if he is consistent. Idtirab makes the addition rejected.
The principle is that ziyadat al-thiqa is accepted unless the narrator is mudtarib.
5
Note the fiqh consequence
Because the addition is not accepted, the Hanafi school does not use this hadith for hand placement; instead, hands are placed below the navel based on other evidence.

And the addition is rejected due to disagreement about it and its extreme individuality. An example of that is the hadith of Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il, from Sufyan, from 'Asim ibn Kulayb, from his father, from Wa'il ibn Hujr, who said: I prayed with the Messenger of God — he placed his right hand on his left hand on his chest. The hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr has been reported regarding placing the right on the left through chains from some of the people of the house of 'Abd al-Jabbar, and Umm 'Abd al-Jabbar, and 'Alqamah ibn Wa'il (14), and 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il, and Kulayb ibn Shihab — all five narrated it from Wa'il ibn Hujr (3). Mu'ammal (3) added in his narration from Sufyan al-Thawri, from 'Asim ibn Kulayb, from his father Kulayb ibn Shihab (5) the phrase: 'on his chest'. However, Mu'ammal was inconsistent in his narration from Sufyan: he narrated it once as 'on his chest', once as 'at his chest', and once without mentioning the addition.

Abu Hatim: sound. Abu Dawud: he was the best of his time. Some said he was a Murji'. Ibn al-Madini: not used as proof when alone. Ibn Sa'd: trustworthy but not many hadiths. Died 137 AH. See ...

(8) This narration is reported by al-Tahawi in Sharh al-Ma'ani 1/196 with the wording: 'I saw the Prophet when he said the takbir for prayer, he raised his hands to his ears.' And in 1/223 with the wording: 'I saw the Messenger of God when he said the takbir for prayer, and when he raised his head'
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage illustrates the principle that an addition (ziyada) by a narrator is rejected when there is disagreement about its authenticity (ikhtilaf) and when it is singular (shiddat al-fardiyya). The case study is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr about placing the right hand on the left hand during prayer. The standard version from multiple chains says 'place his right hand on his left hand', without specifying where. Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il added the phrase 'on his chest' (ala sadrihi). However, Mu'ammal is known to be a weak narrator: he was a hafiz but made many errors, his books were buried so he narrated from memory, and he was inconsistent (mudtarib) in his narration from Sufyan al-Thawri. He sometimes reported 'on his chest', sometimes 'at his chest', and sometimes without any phrase. Therefore, his addition is not accepted. This is a classic example of how the Hanafi method of hadith criticism works: the presence of a strong chain (thubut) is not enough; the narrator must be consistent (not mudtarib). An addition by a trustworthy narrator is generally accepted (ziyadat al-thiqa maqbula), but if the narrator is inconsistent, it is rejected. The Hanafi school does not accept this addition, and therefore the ruling in the Hanafi madhhab is that the hands should be placed beneath the navel, not on the chest, based on other evidence. This passage shows how differences in chains and texts lead to differences in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): An addition in a hadith by a trustworthy narrator that goes beyond what others report
اضطراب (idtirab): Inconsistency in a narrator's transmission of a hadith, causing weakness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why was Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il's addition of 'ala sadrihi' rejected?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran.
B) Because Mu'ammal was inconsistent in his narration.
C) Because the hadith is weak in its chain.
D) Because it is not mentioned in any authentic hadith.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an addition by a narrator is rejected if he is inconsistent (mudtarib), even if he is generally trustworthy.

Evaluating a Ziyada: The Case of 'Upon His Chest'
Textual analysis of a hadith variant and its reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a ziyada in a hadith and apply the Hanafi usul criteria of narrator consistency and chain strength to evaluate its acceptability.

Core Idea
A ziyada from a single unreliable narrator rejected when it contradicts stronger chains.

In Hanafi usul, hadith variants (ziyada) must be scrutinized for reliability. This passage examines the addition 'upon his chest' in the hand-raising hadith. We will see how narrator inconsistency (idṭirāb) and weak supporting chains lead to rejection, following the Hanafi method of prioritizing the majority of trustworthy narrators over a single anomalous report.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ziyada and its original chain
Locate the exact phrase added and the chain that carries it. Here, Mu'ammal added 'upon his chest' in his narration from Sufyan al-Thawri.
The ziyada is a single-word addition that changes the description of hand placement.
2
Assess narrator consistency (idṭirāb)
Check if the narrator transmitted the hadith consistently. Mu'ammal narrated it three different ways: 'upon his chest,' 'by his chest,' and without mention. This idṭirāb weakens his reliability.
Idṭirāb is a serious defect because it shows confusion in the narrator.
3
Examine supporting chains (mutāba'a)
Look for any follow-up chain that agrees with the ziyada. The passage mentions a weak mutāba'a from Ibrahim al-Jawhari, but its narrators (Muhammad ibn Hajar and Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar) are criticized by hadith critics.
A weak mutāba'a does not rescue a weak original chain.
4
Compare with stronger narrations
Contrast the ziyada chain with the majority of reliable narrators who transmitted the same hadith without the addition. The passage notes that trustworthy narrators from Sufyan, 'Asim, and Wa'il did not include the phrase, and their version is preferred.
The Hanafi principle: the majority of trustworthy narrators outweigh a single anomalous narrator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن وائل، وكليب بن شهاب خمستهم رووه عن وائل بن حجر. زاد مؤمل في روايته عن سفيان الثوري، عن عاصم بن كليب عن أبيه كليب بن شهاب جملة: «على صدره». إلا أن مؤملاً اضطرب في روايته عن سفيان فرواه مرة على صدره، ومرة عند صدره، ومرة بدون ذكر الزيادة. وتابع مؤملاً في روايته على صدره متابعة نازلة، إبراهيم بن سعيد الجوهري، عن محمد بن حجر، عن سعيد بن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن أبيه، عن أمه، عن وائل. إلا أنها متابعة ضعيفة، فمحمد بن حجر قال عنه البخاري: كوفي، فيه بعض النظر، وسعيد بن عبد الجبار بن وائل بن حجر قال عنه البخاري فيه نظر، وقال النسائي: ليس بالقوي، وقال ابن عدي: ليس له كثير حديث، وقال ابن حجر ضعیف. ورواية مؤمل مع شدة فرديتها واضطرابه فيها لا تصح لشدة مخالفته بها الرواة عن سفيان الثوري، والرواة عن عاصم بن كليب والرواة عن وائل بن حجر. فقد رواه عن سفيان، عبد الله بن الوليد، ومحمد بن يوسف الفريابي، عن سفيان دون ذكر الزيادة. ورواه عن عاصم بن كليب عبد الله بن إدريس، وشعبة بن الحجاج، وزائدة كلاهما
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text. Wa'il and Kulayb ibn Shihab, five of them narrated it from Wa'il ibn Hujr. Mu'ammal added in his narration from Sufyan al-Thawri, from 'Asim ibn Kulayb from his father Kulayb ibn Shihab, the phrase: 'upon his chest.' However, Mu'ammal was inconsistent in his narration from Sufyan, so he narrated it once as 'upon his chest,' once as 'by his chest,' and once without mentioning the addition. And Mu'ammal was followed in his narration 'upon his chest' by a lower follow-up chain: Ibrahim ibn Sa'id al-Jawhari, from Muhammad ibn Hajar, from Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il from his father, from his mother, from Wa'il. But this follow-up is weak, for Muhammad ibn Hajar - al-Bukhari said about him: Kufan, there is some consideration in him, and Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il ibn Hujr - al-Bukhari said about him: there is consideration, and al-Nasa'i said: not strong, and Ibn 'Adi said: he does not have many hadith, and Ibn Hajar said: weak. And the narration of Mu'ammal, despite its extreme uniqueness and his inconsistency in it, is not authentic due to his strong contradiction of the narrators from Sufyan al-Thawri, and the narrators from 'Asim ibn Kulayb, and the narrators from Wa'il ibn Hujr. For it was narrated from Sufyan by 'Abdullah ibn al-Walid and Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Firyabi, from Sufyan without mentioning the addition. And it was narrated from 'Asim ibn Kulayb by 'Abdullah ibn Idris, Shu'bah ibn al-Hajjaj, and Za'idah, both of them.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith variant concerning the raising of hands during prayer, specifically the addition of 'upon his chest' in the narration of Wa'il ibn Hujr. The author first identifies that the phrase 'upon his chest' appears only in the narration of Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il from Sufyan al-Thawri. However, Mu'ammal is unreliable because he narrated this same hadith in three different ways: once with 'upon his chest', once with 'by his chest', and once without any mention of the chest. This inconsistency (idṭirāb) severely weakens his narration. A follow-up chain (mutāba'a) from Ibrahim al-Jawhari is also examined, but it is weak because two of its narrators, Muhammad ibn Hajar and Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar, are criticized by major hadith critics like al-Bukhari, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Hajar. The author concludes that Mu'ammal's narration is unacceptable because it contradicts the reliable narrations from Sufyan al-Thawri, 'Asim ibn Kulayb, and Wa'il ibn Hujr, who all transmitted the hadith without the addition. This analysis follows the Hanafi method of rigorously scrutinizing hadith variants, especially when a single narrator adds a phrase that is not supported by the majority of trustworthy narrators.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An addition to a hadith text made by one narrator that is not found in other reliable narrations.
متابعة (mutāba'a): A supporting chain that follows the original chain in part, but often with a different route.
اضطراب (idṭirāb): Inconsistency in a narrator's transmission, where a hadith is narrated in contradictory ways.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the addition 'upon his chest' rejected in the hadith of raising hands?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran
B) Because the narrator Mu'ammal was inconsistent and contradicted more reliable narrators
C) Because it is not found in any other hadith
D) Because the Prophet never raised his hands

Key Takeaway
An addition from an unreliable narrator cannot establish a ruling if it contradicts the majority of trustworthy narrators.

Analyzing Weak Chains: The Case of Wa'il ibn Hujr's Ziyada
Critical evaluation of the chain of the ziyada in Wa'il's hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a hadith addition (ziyada) by identifying weak narrators and contradictions with stronger chains, and apply this method to determine its authenticity in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A weak chain and contradiction with authentic narrations invalidate an added phrase (ziyada) even if the base hadith is sound.

Hadith criticism is fundamental to Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The addition of raising hands during prayer (raf' al-yadayn) is a well-known point of ikhtilaf. This lesson unpacks the critical analysis of a specific chain that claimed to support this practice. By examining the narrators and the contradictions, you will learn how the Hanafi school rejects this ziyada and relies on the more authentic transmission without the addition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the weak follow-up (mutaba'a)
The passage begins by presenting a supporting chain for Mu'ammal's narration. Identify the narrators in this chain and note the criticisms leveled against each by hadith critics like al-Bukhari, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Hajar.
Muhammad ibn Hijr and Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar are specifically targeted; their weakness undermines the mutaba'a.
2
Assess the severity of the narrator criticism
Examine the specific wording of the criticisms: 'fihi nadhar' (there is consideration), 'laysa bil-qawi' (not strong), 'da'if' (weak). Understand how these terms rank on the scale of jarh (impugning).
The accumulation of criticism from multiple authorities makes the chain unreliable.
3
Compare with the majority narrators
The author then lists multiple narrators from Sufyan al-Thawri, 'Asim ibn Kulayb, and Wa'il's own family who transmitted the hadith without the ziyada. Count how many narrators are cited and note the consistency among them.
This shows the ziyada is shadh (anomalous) because it contradicts a larger body of reliable transmissions.
4
Apply the principle of idtirab (disturbance)
Mu'ammal's narration is described as having idtirab. Understand that idtirab means the narrator is inconsistent; this further weakens the narration.
Idtirab combined with contradiction makes the narration inadmissible.
5
Conclude on the status of the ziyada
Based on the weak chain and the overwhelming contradiction, the ziyada is rejected. In Hanafi usul, a ziyada from trustworthy narrators is accepted only if it does not contradict stronger narrations. Here it does, so it is not used as evidence.
This analysis directly supports the Hanafi position against raising hands except at the opening takbir.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وتابع مؤملاً في روايته على صدره متابعة نازلة، إبراهيم بن سعيد الجوهري)، عن محمد بن حجر، عن سعيد بن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن أبيه، عن أمه، عن وائل. إلا أنها متابعة ضعيفة، فمحمد بن حجر قال عنه البخاري: كوفي، فيه بعض النظر (۲) ، وسعيد بن عبد الجبار بن وائل بن حجر قال عنه البخاري فيه نظر، وقال النسائي: ليس بالقوي، وقال ابن عدي: ليس له كثير حديث، وقال ابن حجر ضعیف (۳)
ورواية مؤمل مع شدة فرديتها واضطرابه فيها لا تصح لشدة مخالفته بها الرواة عن سفيان الثوري، والرواة عن عاصم بن كليب والرواة عن وائل بن حجر. فقد رواه عن سفيان، عبد الله بن الوليد ()، ومحمد بن يوسف الفريابي)، عن سفيان دون ذكر الزيادة. ورواه عن عاصم بن كليب عبد الله بن إدريس ()، وشعبة بن الحجاج ()، وزائدة ) كلاهما من الركوع يرفع يديه حيال أذنيه». وفي ۲۵۷/١) بلفظ : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا سجد كانت يداه حيال أذنيه».
(۹) ، ومحمد (۲) بن فضيل (۳) ، وزهير (٤) بن معاوية () ، وأبو عوانة)، وقيس بن الربيع ) ، وأبو الأحوص ()، وعبد الواحد بن زياد ، وبشر بن المفضل(۱)، وأبـو إسحاق (۱) جميعهم رووه عن عاصم بن كليب عن كليب دون ذكر الزيادة. ورواه عن وائل (بعض) أهل بيته (۱۲) ، وعلقمة بن وائل منفرداً(۱۳)، وعبد الجبار بن وائل (١٤)، وعلقمة بن وائل، ومولى لهم مقرونين جميعهم رووه عن وائل بن حجر (١٥)
Chapter Three: Difference in Sanad and Matn. And Mu'ammal was followed in his narration upon his chest with a lower follow-up, Ibrahim ibn Sa'id al-Jawhari, from Muhammad ibn Hijr, from Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il from his father, from his mother, from Wa'il. But it is a weak follow-up: Muhammad ibn Hijr, al-Bukhari said about him: Kufi, there is some consideration in him. And Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il ibn Hijr, al-Bukhari said about him: there is consideration, al-Nasa'i said: not strong, Ibn 'Adi said: he does not have many hadiths, and Ibn Hajar said: weak. And the narration of Mu'ammal, despite its extreme uniqueness and his disturbance in it, is not authentic due to his severe contradiction with the narrators from Sufyan al-Thawri, and the narrators from 'Asim ibn Kulayb, and the narrators from Wa'il ibn Hujr. For it was narrated from Sufyan by 'Abdullah ibn al-Walid and Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Firyabi from Sufyan without mentioning the addition. And it was narrated from 'Asim ibn Kulayb by 'Abdullah ibn Idris, Shu'bah ibn al-Hajjaj, and Za'idah... both of them: "from bowing he raised his hands level with his ears." And in 1/257 with the wording: "The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he prostrated, his hands were level with his ears." And Muhammad ibn Fudayl, Zuhayr ibn Mu'awiyah, Abu 'Awanah, Qays ibn al-Rabi', Abu al-Ahwas, 'Abd al-Wahid ibn Ziyad, Bishr ibn al-Mufaddal, and Abu Ishaq, all of them narrated it from 'Asim ibn Kulayb from Kulayb without mentioning the addition. And it was narrated from Wa'il by some of his family members, and 'Alqamah ibn Wa'il alone, and 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il, and 'Alqamah ibn Wa'il, and a freed slave of theirs, all of them narrated it from Wa'il ibn Hujr.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the chains of Wa'il ibn Hujr's hadith concerning raising hands during prayer. The author examines a specific addition (ziyada) found in some narrations and demonstrates its weakness. The text first identifies a weak chain via Mu'ammal and his follower Ibrahim al-Jawhari, pointing out the unreliability of narrators like Muhammad ibn Hijr and Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar. It then shows that the majority of narrators from Sufyan al-Thawri, 'Asim ibn Kulayb, and Wa'il himself transmitted the hadith without this addition, thereby proving the addition is shadh (anomalous) and not accepted. This critical study is foundational for Hanafi fiqh, as the Hanafi school does not accept raising hands during prayer except at the opening takbir, relying on the more authentic version of this hadith without the addition.

Key Terms
متابعة (mutaba'a): A follow-up narration that supports another chain, but here it is described as 'nazila' (lower in rank) and weak.
زيادة (ziyada): An additional phrase in the hadith text that is not found in other reliable versions.
اضطراب (idtirab): The narration is disturbed or inconsistent, making it unreliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why does the author consider Mu'ammal's narration unreliable?
A) Because it has a weak narrator like Muhammad ibn Hijr
B) Because it contradicts the majority of narrators
C) Both A and B
D) Because it is mursal

Key Takeaway
The addition in the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr regarding raising hands is rejected due to weak narrators and contradiction with authentic chains.
