Second: Yahya ibn Sulayman al-Ju'fi. Chapter Three / Disagreement in Isnad and Text. Abu Hatim said about him: 'A shaykh,' and al-Nasa'i said: 'Not trustworthy.' Ibn Hibban mentioned him in al-Thiqat and said: 'He may bring strange narrations.' Despite the uniqueness of these two narrators with this hadith, they contradicted the trustworthy narrators in their narration. Ibn al-Qayyim said about this narration: 'A mistake without doubt, for the incident is one, and the narrators agreed that he did not eat from it, except this anomalous objectionable narration.' The well-known authentic narration is the one reported by a large crowd from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, from Ubaydullah ibn Abdullah ibn Utbah ibn Mas'ud, from Abdullah ibn Abbas, from al-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah al-Laythi, that he gifted to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) a wild donkey while he was at al-Abwa' or Waddan, and he returned it. When he saw the expression on his face, he said: 'We only returned it because we are in ihram.' This narration was reported by Malik in al-Muwatta' (441) in the narration of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, and (53) in the narration of Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Qasim, etc. The impact of this hadith on the disagreement of jurists: This narration contradicting the trustworthy narrators was one of the evidences for those who said it is permissible for the muhrim to eat game if he did not assist, even if it was hunted for him. The detail of the issue was already given in the previous section, so refer to it there.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith variant concerning a muhrim (person in ihram) accepting game meat. The author critiques an anomalous narration (shadhdh) transmitted by two weak narrators, including Yahya ibn Sulayman al-Ju'fi. The majority of authentic narrations from al-Zuhri and others agree that the Prophet returned the gift of a wild donkey because he was in ihram, implying that a muhrim cannot eat game. However, the anomalous narration claims the Prophet did eat, which Ibn al-Qayyim declares a clear error. The author then notes that this weak narration was used by some scholars to permit a muhrim to eat game if he did not actively assist in hunting it. The full debate is referenced as previously discussed. The passage demonstrates how conflicting hadith variants lead to divergent fiqh rulings, and how hadith criticism (jarh wa ta'dil) resolves such conflicts by preferring the sounder narration.

Key Terms
راوية شاذة (riwaya shadhdha): A narration that is anomalous because it contradicts the more reliable narrations from a larger group of trustworthy transmitters.
تفرد (tafarrud): A narrator being the sole transmitter of a hadith or a particular version, which raises suspicion unless the narrator is highly reliable.
شاذ (shādh): A hadith where a trustworthy narrator contradicts another who is more reliable or greater in number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Ibn al-Qayyim consider the anomalous narration about the Prophet eating the donkey a 'mistake'?
A) Because the narrators were all liars.
B) Because the reliable narrators all agreed that the Prophet did not eat, making the contradiction evident.
C) Because the hadith is mursal.
D) Because the chain includes a Shi'i narrator.

Key Takeaway
A shādh narration is identified by its contradiction to stronger chains; it is not a valid basis for legal rulings when reliable narrators agree on the opposite.

Identifying a Munkar Addition in a Fasting Hadith
Textual criticism of a hadith variant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a munkar addition in a hadith and apply the Hanafi usul principle of rejecting tafarrud of a weak narrator.

Core Idea
An additional phrase transmitted by a single weak narrator renders the hadith munkar and unusable as evidence.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith about the concession for fasting during travel. Scholars noticed an extra phrase 'about the traveler' appearing in some transmissions. By analyzing the chain and the transmitter's reliability, we learn how Hanafi usul identifies and excludes anomalous additions to preserve the integrity of prophetic traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and the variant wording
Locate the hadith from Anas about the Prophet's concession for fasting. Note that in some versions, the phrase 'about the traveler' appears twice.
The primary narration mentions the traveler, pregnant, and nursing women.
2
Note the transmitter of the additional phrase
Identify Abu Hilal Muhammad ibn Sulaym as the sole transmitter of the second occurrence of 'about the traveler'.
His tafarrud (singularity) raises suspicion.
3
Evaluate the transmitter's reliability
Check Abu Hilal's biography: truthful but with weakness (saduq fihi lin). His memory is not flawless.
Weakness in precision is critical for accepting additional wording.
4
Apply Hanafi usul principle
In Hanafi usul, a munkar narration (from a weak narrator contradicting stronger transmissions) is rejected. Since other reliable narrators omit this phrase, the addition is deemed munkar.
The principle: 'A weak narrator's tafarrud is rejected when it contradicts the majority.'

The other example: Abu Hilal Muhammad ibn Sulaym singularly transmitted a hadith from Abdullah ibn Suwadah, from Anas ibn Malik from the tribe of Abdullah ibn Ka'b, who said: 'The cavalry of the Messenger of Allah raided us, so I came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while he was having lunch. He said: 'Come near and eat.' I said: 'I am fasting.' He said: 'Sit down, let me tell you about fasting. Allah has lifted half of the prayer for the traveler, and for the traveler, the pregnant, and the nursing women, (He has lifted) the fast...' This narration was reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ibn Sa'd, Ahmad, Abd ibn Humayd, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Fasawi, Ibn Abi Asim, Abdullah ibn (Nu'aym?), Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Tahawi, Ibn Qani', al-Tabari, Ibn Adi, Abu Nu'aym, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Mizzi. Al-Tirmidhi narrated it through this chain but without mentioning the second 'about the traveler.' This wording – i.e., 'about the traveler' – is objectionable (munkar) because of Abu Hilal's uniqueness in it. He is Muhammad ibn Sulaym (Abu Hilal al-Rasibi al-Basri, blind, truthful but with some weakness, died 167 AH).
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents another example of how a sole transmitter's addition leads to a munkar (objectionable) narration. The hadith from Anas reports that the Prophet exempted the traveler from fasting, and in some versions, also the pregnant and nursing women. However, the addition of the second 'about the traveler' (indicating that the concession applies specifically to the traveler, perhaps implying it is exclusive) is transmitted only by Abu Hilal, who is considered truthful but with weakness. Since other more reliable narrations omit this phrase, it is deemed munkar. This hadith is relevant to fiqh because it affects the ruling on fasting for travelers and those with excuses. The Hanafi school, for instance, considers the exemption for the traveler as a concession, but the pregnant and nursing women may have to fast or make up later. The analysis shows how hadith criticism identifies interpolations and ensures the integrity of the sunnah.

Key Terms
منكر (munkar): A hadith that is objectionable because it is transmitted by a weak narrator in contradiction to more reliable narrations.
لفظة (lafza): A specific word or phrase in a hadith; here it refers to the anomalous additional wording 'about the traveler'.
تفرد (tafarrud): The sole transmission of a hadith or a particular wording by one narrator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it contradicts the Quran.
B) Because Abu Hilal was alone in transmitting it and he had some weakness.
C) Because the hadith is about fasting, not prayer.
D) Because all other narrators rejected the entire hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of rejecting munkar additions ensures that only reliably transmitted prophetic words form the basis of legal rulings.

Weak Narrator's Addition (Ziyada) in Hadith: The Case of Abu Hilal
Analyzing a hadith chain difference and its impact on fiqh rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a weak narrator's addition (ziyada) in a hadith chain and apply the principle that such an addition is munkar if it contradicts stronger narrations.

Core Idea
A weak narrator's solitary addition is rejected if it contradicts more reliable chains.

This lesson examines a hadith concerning exemptions from fasting for travelers, pregnant, and nursing women. The focus is on a single word added by the weak narrator Abu Hilal. Understanding how hadith critics evaluate such additions is crucial for usul al-fiqh, as it determines the strength of the evidence and impacts the derivation of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Textual Variation
Locate the specific addition in the hadith text. In this case, Abu Hilal added a second mention of 'traveler' (عن المسافر) that is absent in other chains.
The addition is marked as منكرة (munkar) in the commentary.
2
Assess the Narrator's Reliability
Review the statements of hadith critics about Abu Hilal. The passage quotes numerous scholars who deemed him weak or lenient. Note that even those who considered him trustworthy (e.g., Abu Dawud) still acknowledge mistakes.
Ibn Hibban specifically mentions frequent errors and raising mursal hadith.
3
Compare with Other Chains
The same hadith is reported through other chains (Wahib ibn Khalid and Sufyan al-Thawri) without the addition. These narrators are more reliable.
This comparison is the basis for declaring the addition munkar.
4
Determine the Status of the Addition
Apply the principle: a solitary addition from a weak narrator that contradicts stronger narrations is rejected (munkar). Thus, the proper version of the hadith does not include the extra 'traveler'.
The hadith is still authentic but without that specific wording.
5
Consider the Fiqh Implication
The addition could have been used to argue that the traveler's exemption is separate, but the authentic version groups them. The ruling remains that all three categories are exempt.
This shows how a minor textual variation can affect fiqh if uncritically accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثال الآخر: تفرد أبو هلال مُحَمَّد بن سليم بحَدِيث، عن عَبْد الله بن سوادة، عن أنس بن مالك من بني عَبْد الله بن كعب، قَالَ: «أغارت علينا خيل رَسُوْلُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فأتيت رَسُوْل الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ يتغدى فَقَالَ: «أدن) فكل قلت: إني صائم، قَالَ: «اجلس أحدثك عن الصوم أو الصيام، إن الله وضع عن المسافر شطر الصلاة وعن المسافر والحامل والمرضع الصوم، أو الصيام ...». رَوَاهُ بهذه الرِّوَايَة: ابن أبي شيبة، وابن سعد، وأحمد، وعبد بن حميد، وأبو داود، وابن ماجه، والفسوي، وابن أبي عاصم، وعبد الله بن نعيم، وابن خزيمة، والطحاوي، وابن قانع، والطبراني، وابن عدي، وأبو أحمد، والبيهقي، والمزي. ورواه الترمذي من هَذَا الطريق دون أن يذكر عن المسافر الثانية وهذه اللفظة - أي عن المسافر - منكرة وذلك لتفرد أبي هلال بِهَا وَهُوَ: مُحَمَّد بن سليم الراسبي، وثقه أبو داود، وَكَانَ عَبْد الرَّحْمَن يحدّث عَنْهُ، ولكن كان يحيى لا يحدث عَنْهُ، وَقَالَ ابن سعد: «فِيْهِ ضعف»، وَقَالَ أحمد: «احتمل حديثه»، وأورده البخاري في " الضعفاء الصغير، وَقَالَ أبو حاتم: «محله الصدق وَلَمْ يَكُنْ بذاك المتين»، وَقَالَ أبو زرعة: «لين»، وَقَالَ النسائي: «ليس بقوي»، وساق له ابن عدي في " الكامل عدداً من المناكير ثُمَّ قَالَ: «ولأبي هلال غير ما ذكرت، وفي بعض رواياته ما لا يوافقه الثقات عليه»، وَقَالَ الدَّارَ قُطْنِيّ: «ضعيف»، وأورده ابن حبان في " المجروحين، وَقَالَ: «وَكَانَ أبو هلال شيخاً صدوقاً، إلا أنه كَانَ يخطئ كثيراً من غَيْر تعمد حَتَّى صار يرفع المراسيل ولا يعلم ... وأكثر ما كَانَ حفظه يحدث من فوقع المناكير في حديثه من سوء حفظه وَقَالَ ابن حجر: صدوق فيه لين». فَقَدْ رَوَاهُ وهيب بن خالد، عن عبد الله بن سوادة، عن أبيه، عن أنس، بِهِ عِنْدَ النسائي، والفسوي، والبيهقي. ورواه سفيان الثوري، عن أيوب، عن أبي قلابة، عن أنس بن مالك القشيري، بِهِ عِندَ البخاري في " تاريخه والنسائي، وابن خزيمة، والطبري، والبيهقي.
The other example: Abu Hilal Muhammad ibn Sulaym was alone in narrating a hadith, from Abdullah ibn Sawadah, from Anas ibn Malik of Banu Abdullah ibn Ka'b, who said: 'The cavalry of the Messenger of Allah raided us, so I came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while he was eating lunch. He said: 'Come near and eat.' I said: 'I am fasting.' He said: 'Sit down, I will tell you about fasting. Indeed Allah has removed half of the prayer for the traveler, and (removed) fasting for the traveler, the pregnant woman, and the nursing mother, or fasting...' This narration was reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ibn Sa'd, Ahmad, Abd ibn Humayd, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Fasawi, Ibn Abi Asim, Abdullah ibn Nu'aym, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Tahawi, Ibn Qani', al-Tabarani, Ibn Adi, Abu Ahmad, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Mizzi. Al-Tirmidhi reported it from this chain without mentioning 'traveler' the second time. This word - i.e., 'traveler' - is munkar (rejected) because Abu Hilal is alone in it. He is Muhammad ibn Sulaym al-Rasibi; Abu Dawud declared him trustworthy, and Abd al-Rahman used to narrate from him, but Yahya would not narrate from him. Ibn Sa'd said: 'There is weakness in him.' Ahmad said: 'His hadith is acceptable.' Al-Bukhari included him in al-Du'afa' al-Saghir. Abu Hatim said: 'His status is truthfulness, but he was not that firm.' Abu Zur'ah said: 'Lenient in hadith.' Al-Nasa'i said: 'He is not strong.' Ibn Adi listed several munkar hadiths from him in al-Kamil, then said: 'Abu Hilal has besides what I mentioned, and in some of his narrations, what the trustworthy narrators do not agree with him on.' Al-Daraqutni said: 'Weak.' Ibn Hibban included him in al-Majruhin and said: 'Abu Hilal was a truthful old man, except that he made many mistakes unintentionally, to the point that he would raise mursal narrations without knowing... Most of his memorization was such that he would narrate from memory, and munkar narrations occurred in his hadith due to his poor memory.' Ibn Hajar said: 'Truthful but lenient.' So it was narrated by Wahib ibn Khalid, from Abdullah ibn Sawadah, from his father, from Anas, with the same meaning, according to al-Nasa'i, al-Fasawi, and al-Bayhaqi. And it was narrated by Sufyan al-Thawri, from Ayyub, from Abu Qilabah, from Anas ibn Malik al-Qushayri, with the same meaning, according to al-Bukhari in his Tarikh, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Tabari, and al-Bayhaqi.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a case study in hadith criticism and its effect on fiqh. It presents a hadith about the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that Allah has removed fasting for the traveler, pregnant, and nursing women. The key issue is an addition in one chain: the narrator Abu Hilal ibn Sulaym al-Rasibi added the word 'traveler' a second time, which made the hadith appear to specify the traveler separately. However, this addition is considered munkar (rejected) because Abu Hilal is the only one who reported it, and he is a weak narrator according to many scholars. The author lists many hadith critics who deemed him weak or lenient. In contrast, the same hadith is reported through other chains (Wahib ibn Khalid and Sufyan al-Thawri) without that addition. The juristic implication is that some jurists may have used Abu Hilal's version to argue that the traveler is exempt from fasting, while others rely on the more authentic versions that do not separate the traveler. This shows how a single difference in the chain (a weak narrator's addition) can lead to differing fiqh rulings. The passage does not explicitly state which madhhab held which view, but the implication is that the stronger, more reliable chains are preferable, and thus the ruling based on the addition is weaker.

Key Terms
أبو هلال (Abu Hilal): Muhammad ibn Sulaym al-Rasibi, a narrator considered weak by many critics due to frequent mistakes.
منكر (munkar): A hadith or addition that contradicts stronger narrations due to a weak narrator; rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the addition of 'traveler' in the hadith considered munkar?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran.
B) Because Abu Hilal alone reported it and he is a weak narrator.
C) Because it was transmitted by trustworthy narrators.
D) Because it is a mursal hadith.

Key Takeaway
A weak narrator's solitary addition to a hadith that contradicts stronger chains is rejected as munkar, preserving the integrity of the Sunnah.

Analyzing a Weak Hadith Addition: The Case of Fasting for the Traveler
Analyzing a weak hadith variant and its impact on a fiqh dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a weak addition in a hadith chain and evaluate its impact on a fiqh dispute between schools.

Core Idea
A single weak addition cannot override stronger, more authentic transmissions.

This passage demonstrates how a seemingly minor textual variation in a hadith—a single phrase 'about the traveler'—can lead to a divergent ruling. The author meticulously critiques the chain of the narrator who reports this addition, then shows the fiqh consequence: a minority opinion that forbids fasting for a traveler. As a student of Hanafi usul, you must learn to weigh such textual additions against the broader corpus of authentic narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator and his reliability
Examine the scholarly evaluations of Abu Hilal al-Rasibi. List the major critics and their assessments.
Note the variety of terms: 'weak', 'not strong', 'lenient', etc.
2
Compare the hadith variants
Collect all the chains reported in the passage. Note which ones contain the phrase 'about the traveler' and which do not.
The author counts many chains without the addition.
3
Evaluate the strength of the addition
Assess whether the additional narrator (Abu Hilal) and his sole supporter (Ash'ath ibn Sawwar) are trustworthy. What do the critics say?
Both are considered weak.
4
Assess the impact on the fiqh ruling
How does the addition change the ruling? The first opinion makes fasting invalid; the Hanafi ruling allows it.
The addition transforms a permissible concession into an obligation to break the fast.
5
Determine the tarjih
Given the weakness of the addition, which position is stronger? Why?
The majority, including Hanafis, accept the ruling based on stronger chains and Quran 2:185.

الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن الراسبي، وثقه أبو داود ) ، وَكَانَ عَبْد الرَّحْمَن يحدّث عَنْهُ، ولكن كان يحيى لا يحدث عَنْهُ (۲)، وَقَالَ ابن سعد: «فِيْهِ ضعف» (۳) ، وَقَالَ أحمد: «احتمل حديثه»)، وأورده البخاري في " الضعفاء الصغير (٥)، وَقَالَ أبو حاتم: «محله الصدق وَلَمْ يَكُنْ بذاك المتين» () ، وَقَالَ أبو زرعة: (لين) () ، وَقَالَ النسائي: «ليس بقوي»)، وساق له ابن عدي في " الكامل (۹) عدداً من المناكير ثُمَّ قَالَ: «ولأبي هلال غير ما ذكرت، وفي بعض رواياته ما لا يوافقه الثقات عليه»، وَقَالَ الدَّارَ قُطْنِيّ: (ضعيف)(۱)، وأورده ابن حبان في " المجروحين (۱۱)، وَقَالَ: «وَكَانَ أبو هلال شيخاً صدوقاً، إلا أنه كَانَ يخطئ كثيراً من غَيْر تعمد حَتَّى صار يرفع المراسيل ولا يعلم ... وأكثر ما كَانَ حفظه يحدث من فوقع المناكير في حديثه من سوء حفظه وَقَالَ ابن حجر: صدوق فيه لين»(۱۲). فَقَدْ رَوَاهُ وهيب بن خالد، عن عبد الله بن سوادة، عن أبيه، عن أنس، بِهِ عِنْدَ النسائي)، والفسوي (4) ، والبيهقي ورواه سفيان الثوري، عن أيوب، عن أبي قلابة، عن أنس بن مالك القشيري، بِهِ عِندَ البخاري في " تاريخه والنسائي () ، وابن خزيمة (۱۸) ، (۱۷)، والطبري والبيهقي (۲۰) (١٤) (10) ، (11) (14)
وروي من طرق أخرى عن أيوب، عن أبي قلابة عن رجل من بني عامر، عن أنس في بعض الروايات عن أبي قلابة عن رجل قَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي قريب لي يقال لَهُ أنس بن مالك بِهِ عِنْدَ عَبْد الرزاق (۱) ، وأحمد (۳) ، والبخاري في " تاريخه (V) ،(۳) والنسائي) ، وابن خزيمة ()، والطبراني () ، وللحديث طرق أخرى ) . كُلّ هَذِهِ الروايات ليس فيها لفظة عن المسافر الَّتِي فِي رِوَايَة أَبِي هلال، كَمَا ويكفي لرد هَذِهِ الزيادة حذف الترمذي لها مع أنها ثابتة من طريقه وَقَدْ حسن الْحَدِيث بدونها (۸).
وَقَدْ وجدت لأبي هلال متابعة عَلَى روايته عِنْدَ الطبراني) من طريق أشعث سوار، عن عبد الله بن سوادة، عن أنس بن مالك القشيري به، وهذه المتابعة لا تعضد رِوَايَة أَبِي هلال لضعف أشعث بن سوار فَقَدْ ضعفه أحمد بن حنبل (١٠)، وأبو زرعة (۱۱)، والنسائي (١٢)، والدارقطني (۱۳)
أثر الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء (حكم صوم المسافر)
إِذَا سافر المكلف في رَمَضَان سفراً تتغير بِهِ الأحكام الشرعية، فهل إن فطره من صومه رخصة أم حتم؟ اختلف الفقهاء في هَذَا عَلَى ثلاثة أقوال:
القول الأول:
لا يجوز للمسافر صوم رَمَضَان في سفره، وَلَوْ صامه لَمْ يصح وَعَلَيْهِ قضاؤه.
Chapter Three: Disagreement in chain and text. Al-Rasibi, authenticated by Abu Dawood, and Abd al-Rahman used to narrate from him, but Yahya did not narrate from him. Ibn Sa'd said: 'He has weakness.' Ahmad said: 'His hadith can be tolerated.' Al-Bukhari listed him in al-Du'afa' al-Saghir. Abu Hatim said: 'His position is truthfulness, but he was not strong.' Abu Zur'a said: 'Soft.' Al-Nasa'i said: 'Not strong.' Ibn 'Adi listed numerous munkar hadith for him and said: 'Abu Hilal has other than what I mentioned, and in some of his narrations there is what the trustworthy do not agree with.' Al-Daraqutni said: 'Weak.' Ibn Hibban listed him in al-Majruhin and said: 'Abu Hilal was a truthful shaykh, except that he made many mistakes unintentionally until he began to raise mursal hadith without knowing... and most of his preservation was that he narrated from memory, so munkar occurred in his hadith due to his poor memory.' Ibn Hajar said: 'Truthful, with leniency.' Indeed, Wuhayb ibn Khalid narrated it from 'Abdullah ibn Suwada, from his father, from Anas, as found with al-Nasa'i, al-Fasawi, and al-Bayhaqi. And Sufyan al-Thawri narrated it from Ayyub, from Abu Qilaba, from Anas ibn Malik al-Qushayri, as found with al-Bukhari in his Tarikh, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzayma, al-Tabari, and al-Bayhaqi. And it was narrated through other chains from Ayyub, from Abu Qilaba, from a man from Banu 'Amir, from Anas; in some narrations from Abu Qilaba from a man who said: 'A relative of mine named Anas ibn Malik narrated to me,' as found with 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, al-Bukhari in his Tarikh, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzayma, al-Tabarani, and other chains. All of these narrations do not contain the phrase 'about the traveler' that is in the narration of Abu Hilal, just as it is sufficient to reject this addition that al-Tirmidhi omitted it despite it being proven from his chain, and he graded the hadith hasan without it. And I found for Abu Hilal a follow-up on his narration with al-Tabarani through the chain of Ash'ath ibn Sawwar, from 'Abdullah ibn Suwada, from Anas ibn Malik al-Qushayri, but this follow-up does not support Abu Hilal's narration due to the weakness of Ash'ath ibn Sawwar, for Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu Zur'a, al-Nasa'i, and al-Daraqutni weakened him.
The effect of the hadith on the disagreement of jurists (the ruling on the traveler's fasting)
If a legally responsible person travels in Ramadan a journey that changes the legal rulings, is his breaking of the fast a concession or an obligation? The jurists differed on this into three opinions:
The first opinion:
It is not permissible for the traveler to fast Ramadan during his journey, and if he fasts it, it is not valid and he must make it up.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis demonstrating how discrepancies in hadith chains (sanad) and texts (matn) lead to differences in juristic rulings. The author first examines the narrator Abu Hilal al-Rasibi, citing numerous scholars who critique his reliability, then shows that the version of the hadith containing the phrase 'about the traveler' (عن المسافر) is uniquely reported by him through a weak chain, while all other narrations lack that phrase. The author strengthens this by noting that even the follow-up (mutaba'ah) from Ash'ath ibn Sawwar is weak. Then, the author transitions to the fiqh dispute on fasting for a traveler, presenting the first opinion that it is impermissible and invalid. This opinion likely relies on the hadith with the addition, which the author has shown to be weak. The Hanafi position, by contrast, is that fasting for a traveler is permissible and valid (though one may break the fast). The passage thus illustrates how a weak addition in a hadith can influence a minority opinion, but the stronger, more widely transmitted versions support the majority view.

Key Terms
المسافر (al-musafir): A person undertaking a journey that changes legal rulings (safar al-qasr).
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): An addition in the text of a hadith not found in other authentic narrations.

The Rejected Addition: How a Hadith's Extra Word Led to Three Rulings on Travel Fasting
Analyzing a disputed hadith addition and the resulting three fiqh positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a rejected addition (nakārah) in a hadith, apply the Hanafi usul principle that such an addition cannot override the majority of authentic narrations, and evaluate the resulting three fiqh positions on fasting while traveling.

Core Idea
A single rejected word in a hadith chain created three conflicting rulings—the majority, including the Hanafis, uphold the license to break the fast.

The ruling on fasting while traveling in Ramadan appears simple, yet the hadith evidence contains a critical dispute. In this passage, the author examines a hadith narrated by Abu Hilal with an extra word 'concerning the traveler'. By comparing chains and criticizing the addition, he demonstrates how a subtle textual difference leads to three distinct scholarly opinions. Understanding this case teaches you how Hanafi usul al-hadith principles are applied to resolve apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed hadith and its additional wording
Locate the hadith narrated by Abu Hilal that contains the phrase 'عن المسافر' (concerning the traveler). Compare this with the many other narrations from Ayyub, Abu Qilabah, and Anas that lack this word. Note that this addition changes the apparent command.
The addition makes the hadith seem to command breaking the fast specifically for travelers.
2
Examine the author's method of rejecting the addition
The author points out that al-Tirmidhi transmitted the hadith but omitted the addition, and declared the hadith hasan without it. He also notes that the only follow-up narration for Abu Hilal is through Ash'ath ibn Sawwar, who is declared weak by major hadith critics. Thus, the addition is odd (nakārah) and rejected.
This is an application of the hadith criticism principle that a weak addition cannot override authentic narrations.
3
List the three scholarly opinions on fasting while traveling
State each opinion: (1) Zahiris and Imamis say fasting is invalid and prohibited. (2) Ahmad says breaking is a license but breaking is better. (3) Majority (including Abu Hanifa) say breaking is a license but fasting is better if no harm.
The first opinion relies solely on the rejected addition.
4
Link each opinion to its hadith evidence
The first opinion uses the addition as evidence that the traveler must break the fast. The second and third opinions rely on the authentic narration without the addition, which permits fasting. The author's critique shows the addition is unreliable, leaving the majority view as the better evidenced.
Without the addition, the hadith does not command breaking; it merely permits it.
5
Determine the Hanafi position and the tarjih
The Hanafi school follows the third opinion: breaking the fast is a license (rukhsah), but fasting is better if no harm. This is because the general obligation of Ramadan remains, and the supposed evidence for obligation is weak. The tarjih favors the majority due to the weakness of the addition.
The Hanafi position prioritizes the stronger evidence and the principle that a license does not become an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وروي من طرق أخرى عن أيوب، عن أبي قلابة عن رجل من بني عامر، عن أنس في بعض الروايات عن أبي قلابة عن رجل قَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي قريب لي يقال لَهُ أنس بن مالك بِهِ عِنْدَ عَبْد الرزاق، وأحمد، والبخاري في " تاريخه"، والنسائي، وابن خزيمة، والطبراني، وللحديث طرق أخرى. كُلّ هَذِهِ الروايات ليس فيها لفظة عن المسافر الَّتِي فِي رِوَايَة أَبِي هلال، كَمَا ويكفي لرد هَذِهِ الزيادة حذف الترمذي لها مع أنها ثابتة من طريقه وَقَدْ حسن الْحَدِيث بدونها.
وَقَدْ وجدت لأبي هلال متابعة عَلَى روايته عِنْدَ الطبراني من طريق أشعث بن سوار، عن عبد الله بن سوادة، عن أنس بن مالك القشيري به، وهذه المتابعة لا تعضد رِوَايَة أَبِي هلال لضعف أشعث بن سوار فَقَدْ ضعفه أحمد بن حنبل، وأبو زرعة، والنسائي، والدارقطني.
أثر الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء (حكم صوم المسافر)
إِذَا سافر المكلف في رَمَضَان سفراً تتغير بِهِ الأحكام الشرعية، فهل إن فطره من صومه رخصة أم حتم؟ اختلف الفقهاء في هَذَا عَلَى ثلاثة أقوال:
القول الأول:
لا يجوز للمسافر صوم رَمَضَان في سفره، وَلَوْ صامه لَمْ يصح وَعَلَيْهِ قضاؤه. وإلى هَذَا ذهب الظاهرية، والإمامية.
القول الثاني:
إن إفطار المسافر في رَمَضَان رخصة إن شاء أفطر وإن شاء صام، لكن الفطر أفضل. وإليه ذهب أحمد.
القول الثالث:
إن الفطر رخصة، والصيام أفضل بشرط عدم الضرر والتلف. وبه قَالَ جمهور الفقهاء. وإليه ذهب أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ، ومالك، والشافعي، والزيدية.
واستدل أصحاب المذهب الأول بزيادة «المسافر» الثانية في حديث أبي هلال، وَقَدْ بينا نكارة هَذِهِ اللفظة فَلَمْ يصح الاحتجاج بها.
Chapter Three / Difference in Chain and Text. It was narrated through other chains from Ayyub, from Abu Qilabah, from a man from Banu Amir, from Anas; in some narrations from Abu Qilabah, from a man who said: A relative of mine named Anas ibn Malik narrated to me... at 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, al-Bukhari in his Tarikh, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Tabarani, and the hadith has other chains. All these narrations do not contain the word 'concerning the traveler' that is in the narration of Abu Hilal. And it is sufficient to reject this addition that al-Tirmidhi omitted it although it is established through his chain, and he declared the hadith hasan without it. And I found a follow-up for Abu Hilal's narration with al-Tabarani from the path of Ash'ath ibn Sawwar, from 'Abdullah ibn Sawadah, from Anas ibn Malik al-Qushayri. This follow-up does not support Abu Hilal's narration due to the weakness of Ash'ath ibn Sawwar, as Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu Zur'ah, al-Nasa'i, and al-Daraqutni declared him weak. The effect of the hadith on the difference of jurists (ruling on fasting of the traveler): When a legally responsible person travels in Ramadan a journey that changes legal rulings, is his breaking of the fast a license or an obligation? The jurists differed on this into three opinions: The first opinion: It is not permissible for the traveler to fast Ramadan during his travel, and if he fasts it is not valid and he must make it up. The Zahiris and Imamis held this. The second opinion: The traveler's breaking of the fast in Ramadan is a license; if he wishes he breaks and if he wishes he fasts, but breaking is better. Ahmad held this. The third opinion: Breaking is a license, but fasting is better on condition of no harm or loss. The majority of jurists said this, and Abu Hanifah, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and the Zaydis held it. The proponents of the first opinion used as evidence the additional word 'traveler' in the hadith of Abu Hilal, but we have shown the oddity of this word, so it is not valid to argue with it.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a dispute analysis (ikhtilaf) showing how a difference in hadith chain and text leads to different fiqh rulings. The author first examines the hadith narrated by Abu Hilal which contains the addition 'concerning the traveler' (عن المسافر). He compares it with many other narrations from Ayyub, Abu Qilabah, and Anas which lack this addition. He points out that even al-Tirmidhi, who transmitted the hadith, omitted the addition, and he declared the hadith hasan without it. Furthermore, the only follow-up narration for Abu Hilal is through Ash'ath ibn Sawwar, who is weak. Thus the addition is rejected (munkar). The fiqh issue is whether a traveler must break the fast in Ramadan, or may choose. Three opinions: (1) Zahiris and Imamis: fasting is invalid and prohibited. (2) Ahmad: breaking is a license but better. (3) Majority (including Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i): breaking is a license but fasting is better if no harm. The first group relied on the rejected addition; without it, the hadith supports the majority view. The Hanafi position is the third: fasting is superior, maintaining the general obligation of Ramadan unless breaking is needed to avoid harm.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A dispensatory ruling that permits an otherwise prohibited or disliked action under specific circumstances.
حتم (hatm): An obligatory ruling that must be followed without choice.
نكارة (nakārah): A term in hadith criticism indicating an odd or unacceptable element in the text or chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling on fasting while traveling in Ramadan?
A) Fasting is prohibited and invalid.
B) Breaking the fast is a license but fasting is better if no harm.
C) Breaking the fast is obligatory.
D) Both fasting and breaking are equally permissible.

Key Takeaway
A single weak addition in a hadith can create conflicting rulings, but Hanafi usul protects the strength of the majority by rejecting odd additions and upholding the authentic core.

Definition of al-Mudraj: Linguistic and Terminological
Defines the term 'Mudraj' linguistically and technically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Mudraj linguistically and technically, and distinguish it from other hadith defects using Hanafi usul criteria.

Core Idea
Al-Mudraj is a hadith with an unmarked narrator addition; its presence weakens the hadith as a legal proof.

In this lesson, we examine the precise definition of al-Mudraj—a term crucial for evaluating hadith authenticity in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Understanding its linguistic roots helps grasp why a mudraj hadith is considered unreliable unless the addition is clearly separated. The passage defines the term both lexically and technically, and explains the continuity between the two meanings.

Guided Path
1
Trace the linguistic root
Examine the triliteral root d-r-j and its core meanings: folding and inserting. Understand how the passive participle 'mudraj' derives from 'adraja' (to fold/insert).
Ibn Fāris confirms the root indicates passage or entry.
2
Identify the technical definition
State the hadith science definition: a hadith that contains an increase (ziyada) in its chain (sanad) or text (matn) that is not originally from the Prophet, inserted by a narrator without clarifying the addition.
The passage gives two phrasings: 'what contains an increase not from it' and 'the hadith known to have an addition from a narrator without clarification'.
3
Connect linguistic and technical meanings
Understand how the technical term retains the literal sense: the narrator either 'folded' the explanation (failed to clarify) or 'inserted' one hadith into another. The term does not become metaphorical.
The passage concludes that the technical usage remains on the original linguistic وضع.
4
Apply to Hanafi usul
Recognize that a mudraj hadith is considered weak (da'if) as a proof (dalil) in Hanafi usul unless the addition is identified and isolated. The original part may still be used if separable.
This affects istinbat: a mudraj hadith cannot support a ruling unless the interpolation is removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الأول: تعريفه
المُدْرَجُ لغة - بضم الميم وفتح الراء - اسم مفعول من (أدرج)، تقول: أدرجت الكتاب إذا طويته وتقول: أدرجت الميت في القبر إذا أدخلته فيه، وتقول: أدرجت الشيء في الشيء إذا أدخلته فيه وضمنته إياه).
قال ابن فارس: «الدال والراء والجيم أصل واحد يدل عَلَى مُضِي الشيء والمُضِي في الشيء».
ودَرَجَ الشيء في الشيء: أدخله في ثناياه ) ، ومنه: الدَّرَجَة وَهِيَ المرقاة؛ لأنها توصل إلى الدخول في الشيء حسياً أو معنوياً، فهي من باب تسمية السبب بنتيجته. وفي اصطلاح الْمُحَدِّثِيْنَ: هُوَ ما كانت فيه زيادة ليست مِنْهُ.
أو هُوَ الْحَدِيث الذي يعرف أن في سنده أو متنه زيادة ليست منه، وإنما من أحد الرُّوَاة من غَيْر توضيح لهذه الزيادة.
العلاقة بين المعنى اللغوي والاصطلاحي:
وجدنا أن معنى الفعل الثلاثي المجرد (دَرَجَ) يدور عَلَى أمرين:
١. طوي الشيء.
٢. إدخال الشيء في الشيء.
وكأنَّ المُدرج طوى البيان، فَلَمْ يوضح تفصيل الأمر في الْحَدِيث. أو كأنه أدخل الْحَدِيث فِي الْحَدِيث، فالاستعمال الاصطلاحي باقٍ عَلَى الوضع اللغوي الأول، وَلَمْ يخرج إلى المجاز.
First Requirement: Its Definition. Al-Mudraj linguistically - with a dammah on the meem and a fatha on the raa - is a passive participle from (adraja). You say: adrajtu al-kitāb when you fold it, and you say: adrajtu al-mayyita fī al-qabri when you insert it into it, and you say: adrajtu al-shay'a fī al-shay'i when you insert it into it and include it. Ibn Fāris said: 'The dāl, rā', and jīm form a single root indicating the passage of a thing and the passage into a thing.' And daraja al-shay' fī al-shay': inserted it into its folds, and from it: al-darajah which is the step, because it leads to entering into a thing, sensibly or meaningfully, so it is from the category of naming the cause by its result. In the terminology of the hadith scholars: it is that which contains an increase that is not from it. Or it is the hadith which is known that in its chain or text there is an increase that is not from it, but rather from one of the narrators without clarification of this increase. The relationship between the linguistic and terminological meaning: We found that the meaning of the simple triliteral verb (daraja) revolves around two matters: 1. Folding a thing. 2. Inserting a thing into a thing. It is as if the mudraj folded the explanation, so he did not clarify the detail of the matter in the hadith. Or as if he inserted the hadith into the hadith, so the terminological usage remains on the original linguistic usage, and did not depart into metaphor.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the term 'al-Mudraj' in hadith terminology. The author begins with the linguistic meaning, tracing it to the root 'daraja' which conveys folding or inserting. The passive participle 'mudraj' indicates something that has been folded or inserted. Ibn Fāris confirms the root meaning of passage and entry. From this, the word 'darajah' (step) is derived because it leads to entering something. The technical definition given: a hadith in which there is an addition that is not part of it, either in the chain (sanad) or text (matn), inserted by a narrator without clarification of the addition. The author then connects the linguistic and technical meanings: the mudraj narrator either 'folded' the explanation (i.e., did not make clear the distinction) or 'inserted' one hadith into another. Thus the technical term remains true to the literal sense without metaphorical extension. In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, identifying mudraj hadith is crucial for determining the authenticity of reports used as legal proofs, since a mudraj hadith is considered weak unless the addition is clearly distinguished.

Key Terms
المُدْرَج (al-mudraj): A hadith in which there is an increase (from a narrator) that is not part of the original hadith, without clarifying that increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the terminological definition of al-Mudraj in hadith science?
A) A hadith whose chain is broken
B) A hadith containing an increase from a narrator without clarification
C) A hadith that contradicts stronger narrations
D) A hadith with a hidden defect in the chain

Key Takeaway
Al-Mudraj is a hadith with an unclarified narrator addition; its detection is essential for sound hadith criticism in Hanafi usul.

Definition and Scope of Idraj
Definition and critique of idraj classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define idraj (inserted text) and critique the limitation of its occurrence to the end of the hadith.

Core Idea
Idraj can occur at the beginning, middle, or end of the text, and even in the chain.

Hadith scholars and jurists rely on sound transmissions for legal rulings. When a narrator's own words are mixed with the Prophet's ﷺ speech without distinction, it creates idraj. This lesson unpacks the definition of idraj and corrects a common misconception that it only happens at the end of a hadith.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Idraj is inserting a narrator's speech into the hadith without separation, causing confusion.
2
Analyze Ibn al-Salah's restriction
He said idraj occurs 'after the hadith' (at the end).
3
Identify the critique
The author argues it can also be at the beginning, middle, and in the chain.
4
See the evidence
The author refers to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's practice and gives an example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
المطلب الثاني: أنواعه
يتفق الباحثون والكتاب في مجال علوم الْحَدِيث عَلَى جعل المدرج عَلَى أنواع. لكن تقسيمهم لهذه الأنواع يختلف زيادة ونقصاً، كما يختلف باعتبار الحيثيات التي ينبني عَلَيْهَا ذَلِكَ التقسيم. وهكذا نجد الحافظ ابن الصَّلاحِ يصدر كلامه عن المدرج بقوله: «وَهُوَ أقسام، مِنْهَا ما أدرج في حَدِيث رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كلام بعض رواته بأن يذكر الصَّحَابِيّ أو مَنْ بعده عقيب ما يرويه من الحَدِيث كلاماً من عِنْدَ نفسه، فيرويهِ مَنْ بعده موصولاً بالحديث غَيْر فاصل بينهما بذكر قائله، فيلتبس الأمر فِيْهِ عَلَى من لا يعلم حقيقة الحال، ويتوهم أن الجميع عن رَسُول الله (۱).
فنراه قيد وقوع الإدراج بكونه عقب الْحَدِيث، والحق أن هذا التنظيـر خـلاف الواقع، وإذا كَانَ غالب الإدراج أن يقع عقب الحَدِيث، فليس هـذا مـسـوعـاً لـحـصـر الإدراج بِهِ، فنجد أنه قد يقع في أول الْحَدِيث كَمَا يقع وسطه وآخره. زد على أنه يقع في الإسناد أَيْضاً لا كَمَا يوهم كلام ابن الصَّلاح من انحصاره بالمتن فقط. وعلى هَذَا صنيع الْخَطِيب البغدادي في كتابه " الفصل للوصل المدرج في النقل وتأسيساً على ما مضى يمكننا أن نقسم الإدراج من حَيْثُ مكان وقوعه إلى نوعين:
النوع الأول: الإدراج في المتن.
النوع الثاني: الإدراج في السند.
النوع الأول: الإدراج في المتن:
وَهُوَ أن تقع الزيادة في متن الْحَدِيث دون إسناده.
ويمكن تقسيم هَذَا النوع باعتبار مكان وقوعه من المثن إلى ثلاثة أقسام:
١. أن يقع الإدراج في أول الْمَثْن. ٢. أن يقع الإدراج في وسط المثن.
٣. أن يقع الإدراج في آخر المثن.
فمثال ما وقع الإدراج في أول الْمَثْن حَدِيث أبي هُرَيْرَة رضي الله عنه عن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أسبغوا الوضوء، ويل للأعقاب من النار».
فرواه الْخَطِيب البغدادي في كتابه " الفصل من طريق أبي قطن وشبابة - فرقهما عن شعبة، عن مُحَمَّد بن زياد، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، به.
فقوله: «أسبغوا الوضوء» مدرج من كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة، نص عَلَى هَذَا الْخَطِيْبِ وغيره فَقَالَ: «وَهِمَ أبو قطن عمرو بن الهيثم وشبابة بن سوار في روايتهما هَذَا الْحَدِيث عن شعبة عَلَى ما سقناه، وذلك أن قوله: «أسبغوا الوضوء» كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة، وقوله: «ويل للأعقاب من النار» كلام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم.
وَقَدْ رَوَى هَذَا الْحَدِيث عن شعبة عامة أصحابه فبينوا أن هَذِهِ الزيادة من كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة، وهم: 
١. آدم بن أبي إياس، عِنْدَ البخاري. 
٢. حجاج بن مُحَمَّد، عِنْدَ أَحْمَد. 
٣. أبو داود الطيالسي، كما في " مسنده". 
٤. عاصم بن علي، عِنْدَ الْخَطِيب. 
٥. علي بن الجعد، عِنْدَ الْخَطِيب. 
٦. عيسى بن يونس، عِنْدَ الْخَطِيْب.
Chapter Three / Disagreement in Chain and Text
Section Two: Its Types
Researchers and writers in the field of hadith sciences agree on classifying mudraj into types. But their division of these types differs in increase and decrease, and also differs according to the considerations upon which that division is based. Thus we find al-Hafiz Ibn al-Salah begins his speech about mudraj saying: 'It has categories, among them what is inserted into the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, from the speech of some of its narrators, in that the Companion or one after him mentions immediately after what he narrates of the hadith speech from himself, then the one after him narrates it connected to the hadith without a separator between them mentioning its speaker, so the matter becomes confused for one who does not know the true state of affairs, and he imagines that all of it is from the Messenger of Allah.' So we see that he restricted the occurrence of idraj to being after the hadith, and the truth is that this theorizing is contrary to reality. Even if most idraj occurs after the hadith, this does not permit restricting idraj to it. We find that it may occur at the beginning of the hadith as it occurs in its middle and end. Add to that it occurs in the chain as well, not as Ibn al-Salah's statement implies by confining it to the text only. And upon this is the practice of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi in his book 'al-Fasl lil-Wasl al-Mudraj fi al-Naqli.' And based on what has passed, we can divide idraj in terms of its place of occurrence into two types:
Type One: Idraj in the text.
Type Two: Idraj in the chain.
Type One: Idraj in the text:
It is that the addition occurs in the text of the hadith, not in its chain.
This type can be divided in terms of its place of occurrence in the text into three categories:
1. Idraj occurs at the beginning of the text.
2. Idraj occurs in the middle of the text.
3. Idraj occurs at the end of the text.
An example of idraj occurring at the beginning of the text is the hadith of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'Perform the ablution thoroughly; woe to the heels from the Fire.'
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi narrated it in his book 'al-Fasl' via the path of Abu Qatan and Shababa - both from Shu'bah, from Muhammad bin Ziyad, from Abu Hurairah, with it.
His statement: 'Perform the ablution thoroughly' is mudraj from the speech of Abu Hurairah. Al-Khatib and others explicitly stated this, saying: 'Abu Qatan Amr ibn al-Haytham and Shababa ibn Sawwar erred in their narration of this hadith from Shu'bah as we have related it, because his statement: ''Perform the ablution thoroughly'' is the speech of Abu Hurairah, and his statement: ''Woe to the heels from the Fire'' is the speech of the Prophet, peace be upon him.'
And the majority of Shu'bah's companions narrated this hadith from him and clarified that this addition is from the speech of Abu Hurairah. They are:
1. Adam ibn Abi Iyas, according to al-Bukhari.
2. Hajjaj ibn Muhammad, according to Ahmad.
3. Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi, as in his 'Musnad'.
4. Asim ibn Ali, according to al-Khatib.
5. Ali ibn al-Ja'd, according to al-Khatib.
6. Isa ibn Yunus, according to al-Khatib.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the types of idraj (inserted text) in hadith, a crucial concept for scholars of usul who need to evaluate hadith evidence. The author begins by noting that while scholars agree on classifying mudraj, their categories differ. He then critiques Ibn al-Salah's definition, which restricts idraj to occurring after the hadith (at the end). The author argues that idraj can occur at the beginning, middle, or end of the matn (text), and also in the isnad (chain). He supports this by referencing al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's work. The author then provides a formal division: idraj in the matn (text) and idraj in the isnad (chain). For matn idraj, he further subdivides into beginning, middle, and end. He gives a concrete example: the hadith 'Aghsilu al-wudu', waylun li'l-a'qabi min al-nar' (Perform ablution thoroughly, woe to the heels from the Fire). The phrase 'Aghsilu al-wudu'' was inserted by Abu Hurairah himself, not from the Prophet. Al-Khatib pointed out the error of two narrators who transmitted it as one continuous hadith. The author lists six reliable narrators who clarified this insertion. This example shows how idraj can mislead if not identified, affecting legal rulings derived from hadith.

Key Terms
الإدراج (al-idraj): Inserting speech from a narrator into the hadith text or chain without clear separation, causing confusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is an example of idraj occurring at the beginning of the hadith text?
A) The phrase 'Aghsilu al-wudu'' inserted before 'Waylun li'l-a'qabi min al-nar'.
B) The phrase 'Waylun li'l-a'qabi min al-nar' inserted after 'Aghsilu al-wudu''.
C) The name of a narrator inserted in the chain.
D) The Prophet's saying inserted in the middle of a Companion's statement.

Key Takeaway
Idraj is not only at the end; it can occur at any part of the matn or in the isnad, so scholars must compare narrations to detect it.

Types of Idraj: Location in Text and Chain with Example
Classification of idraj and illustrative example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify idraj by location (matn/isnad and subtypes within matn) and identify the idraj in the hadith of Abu Hurairah.

Core Idea
Idraj in the matn is divided into three locations: beginning, middle, end; the hadith of Abu Hurairah illustrates beginning idraj.

Having understood the definition of idraj, we now explore its types based on where the insertion occurs. The text of a hadith can be affected at any point, and the chain can also contain inserted elements. This lesson provides a detailed classification and a concrete example to solidify the concept.

Guided Path
1
Recognize two main types
Idraj in matn (text) and idraj in isnad (chain).
2
Note three subtypes for matn idraj
Beginning, middle, end.
3
Examine the example
Hadith of Abu Hurairah has idraj at the beginning: 'أسبغوا الوضوء' is inserted.
4
Understand detection method
Comparison of narrations: majority of reliable narrators did not include the inserted phrase.

Weighing Textual Variants: The List of Narrators Without Idraj
A catalog of narrators who transmitted a hadith without an inserted phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify narrators who transmitted a hadith without an additional phrase and explain why the absence of idraj in multiple chains strengthens the authenticity of that version in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The absence of an interpolation across many independent chains is strong evidence that the original hadith did not contain it.

This passage shows how Hanafi scholars use the multiplicity of narrators to distinguish between inserted text (idraj) and the original wording. By listing transmitters who confined the narration to 'the male' without adding 'the raising and the two females', the author builds a case that the shorter version is the authentic one. This is a crucial method in hadith criticism for deriving correct rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognise that the passage highlights a textual difference: some narrators added a phrase (idraj) while others did not. The list focuses on those who omitted it.
The addition is described as 'الرفع والأنثيين' – likely a reference to a specific legal ruling.
2
Analyze the significance of the list
Note that the author lists 18 companions of Hisham who transmitted without the addition. This multiplicity (tawatur or istifadah) strengthens the version without idraj.
In Hanafi usul, a widely transmitted text (mashhur) is given preference over a solitary one.
3
Apply the concept of idraj
Understand that idraj is an interpolation. The absence of the addition in these chains suggests it was not part of the original hadith.
The term idraj is critical: it can invalidate or weaken a narration if it is proven to be inserted.
4
Evaluate the reliability of the chains
Consider that the list includes names of well-known narrators like Sufyan al-Thawri and Yahya al-Qattan, indicating that the transmission without idraj is through trustworthy sources.
This further bolsters the authenticity of the shorter version.
5
Connect to ruling derivation
Realize that the preferred version of the hadith will affect the fiqh ruling. The absence of the addition may support the Hanafi position on the issue (e.g., raising hands in prayer or inheritance shares).
The exact ruling is not given here, but the method of weighing narrations is universal.

Commentary
This passage is from a chapter on disagreements in chain and text of hadith. The author lists the companions (students) of the narrator Hisham who transmitted a specific hadith from him, but they confined the narration to the mention of 'the male' without adding the phrase about 'raising and the two females'. This indicates a textual difference: some narrators included an additional part. The 'raising and the two females' likely refers to a specific legal detail—perhaps related to raising hands in prayer or inheritance shares. The author then begins discussing the narration of Ayyub, noting that Yazid ibn Zari' narrated from Ayyub, and there is disagreement about Yazid's version. Most narrators from Yazid transmit without the insertion. The passage is a catalog of chains to establish the prevalence of one version over another, which is fundamental in weighing conflicting narrations for deriving rulings.

Key Terms
الإدراج (al-idraj): Insertion or interpolation of additional words into the hadith text that are not part of the original narration.
المرفوع (al-marfu'): A hadith attributed to the Prophet Muhammad, raised to him.
الذكر (al-dhakar): The male; in this context, the word 'male' in the hadith text.
التواتر (al-tawatur): A transmission by such a large number of narrators that collusion to fabricate is impossible.
الشهرة (al-shuhrah): Widespread but not necessarily tawatur; still strong in Hanafi weighting.

Idraj in the Hadith of Wudu from Touching the Penis
Critical examination of idraj in the hadith of wudu from touching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of idraj to evaluate conflicting narrations and derive the Hanafi ruling on wudu from touching the penis.

Core Idea
Idraj weakens a narration; the preponderant version of the hadith limits wudu to touching the penis alone.

This passage delves into the technical hadith criticism of the well-known hadith of Busrah bint Safwan (رضي الله عنها) regarding wudu from touching the penis. The dispute centers on whether extra words—'testicles' and 'anus'—were inserted (idrāj) by some narrators. Understanding this analysis is key for the Hanafi school's ruling that only touching the penis necessitates wudu, not other organs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base hadith and its variants
The hadith of Busrah states: 'If one of you touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' Some narrations add 'or his two testicles' or 'or his anus'. Identify which version is the base and which has additions.
The base version is reported by the majority of Hisham's students.
2
Understand the concept of idraj
Idraj occurs when a narrator inserts his own words into the hadith text, mistaking them for part of the original. Scholars detect idraj by comparing multiple chains.
3
Examine the majority narration from Hisham
The passage lists eighteen companions of Hisham who narrated without idraj. This indicates the widespread nature of the shorter version.
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi affirmed this.
4
Evaluate the conflicting narrations from Ayyub and others
Most of Ayyub's students transmitted without idraj, except Abu Kamil al-Jahdari. Similarly, Ibn Jurayj's narration with idraj was ruled as such by al-Daraqutni and Ibn Hajar.
The majority principle (kathrah) supports the shorter version.
5
Assess the strength of the idraj narrations
Hadith critics ruled the idraj narrations as weak (shadhdh) due to opposition to the majority. This preponderance (tarjih) establishes the authentic text.
The Hanafi position relies on this tarjih.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن فهؤلاء ثمانية عشر نفساً من أصحاب هشام رووه عنه مقتصرين على الذكر من غير إدراج للرفع والأنثيين في المرفوع منه. أما رواية أيوب التي أرجأنا الكلام عنها، فقد روى الحديث عن أيوب يزيد بن زريع واختلف على يزيد في روايته وأكثر الرواة عنه يروونه عنه، عن أيوب، عن هشام من غير إدراج وهم: أحمد بن عبيد الله العنبري عند الدارقطني. أحمد بن المقدام عند الدارقطني. عبيد الله بن عمر القواريري. عمرو بن علي عند الخطيب. لذا عد الخطيب أيوب ممن بين الإدراج في الحديث. في حين أن أبا كامل الجحدري رواه عن يزيد بن زريع، عن أيوب مدرجاً، كما أخرجه الطبراني، فعاد الخطيب فعد أيوب ممن أدرج الحديث. فالذي يترجح رواية الجمع عن أيوب، فيعد أيوب ممن بين الإدراج، وبالتالي فتترجح رواية الجمع ممن بين الإدراج في روايتهم عن هشام بن عروة، ويؤيد هذا قول الخطيب: روى كافة أصحاب هشام بن عروة عنه حديث الوضوء من مس الذكر خاصة، ولم يذكر أحد منهم الأنثيين والرفغين في روايته. وقد حكم الخطيب البغدادي على عبد الحميد بن جعفر بتفرده بالإدراج عن هشام بن عروة. واعترض عليه الحافظ العراقي برواية أبي كامل الجحدري التي مضى الكلام عليها، وبرواية ابن جريج عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن مروان، عن بسرة بلفظ: «إذا أحدكم ذكره أو أنثييه». والذي يبدو أن حكم الخطيب حكم مقيد لا مطلق والمقيد ذهني إذ أنه تفرد من طريق يعتد بها، أما هاتان الطريقان فلا اعتماد عليهما لما يأتي: أما رواية أبي كامل فقد بينا أنه خالف فيها جمهور الرواة عن أيوب، فلا يلتفت إليها. وأما رواية ابن جريج فقد حكم الدارقطني والحافظ ابن حجر عليها بالإدراج أيضاً. وهناك طريقان آخران عن هشام بن عروة ورد فيهما الإدراج فقد روى محمد بن دينار، عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن بسرة هذا الحديث مدرجاً، وروايته أخرجها الطبراني والدارقطني.
Chapter Three: Difference in Sanad and Matn. So these are eighteen individuals from the companions of Hisham who narrated it from him, restricting it to the penis without inclusion of the anus and the two testicles in the raised part. As for the narration of Ayyub, which we postponed discussing, indeed Yazid ibn Zuray' narrated the hadith from Ayyub, and there is difference over Yazid in his narration, and most of the narrators from him narrate from him, from Ayyub, from Hisham without inclusion: they are Ahmad ibn 'Ubaydullah al-'Anbari (according to al-Daraqutni), Ahmad ibn al-Miqdam (according to al-Daraqutni), 'Ubaydullah ibn 'Umar al-Qawariri, 'Amr ibn 'Ali (according to al-Khatib). Hence al-Khatib considered Ayyub among those who clarified the inclusion in the hadith. Whereas Abu Kamil al-Jahdari narrated it from Yazid ibn Zuray', from Ayyub, with inclusion, as al-Tabarani recorded, so al-Khatib reversed and counted Ayyub among those who inserted the inclusion. So what is preponderant is the narration of the majority from Ayyub, so Ayyub is counted among those who clarified the inclusion, and thus the narration of the majority of those who clarified the inclusion in their narration from Hisham ibn 'Urwah is preponderant. This is supported by al-Khatib's statement: 'All the companions of Hisham ibn 'Urwah narrated from him the hadith of wudu from touching the penis specifically, and none of them mentioned the two testicles and the anus in his narration.' And al-Khatib al-Baghdadi ruled that 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far was unique in including (the insertion) from Hisham ibn 'Urwah. Al-Hafiz al-'Iraqi objected to him with the narration of Abu Kamil al-Jahdari, which was already discussed, and with the narration of Ibn Jurayj from Hisham ibn 'Urwah, from his father, from Marwan, from Busrah with the wording: 'If one of you touches his penis or his two testicles.' And it appears that al-Khatib's ruling is a restricted ruling, not absolute, and the restriction is mental, because it is uniqueness from a path that is relied upon. As for these two paths, there is no reliance upon them for the following: As for the narration of Abu Kamil, we have shown that he opposed the majority of the narrators from Ayyub, so attention is not paid to it. As for the narration of Ibn Jurayj, al-Daraqutni and al-Hafiz ibn Hajar ruled it as having insertion as well. And there are two other paths from Hisham ibn 'Urwah in which insertion occurs: Muhammad ibn Dinar narrated from Hisham ibn 'Urwah, from his father, from Busrah, this hadith with insertion, and his narration was recorded by al-Tabarani and al-Daraqutni.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the hadith on wudu from touching the penis, focusing on whether the mention of 'testicles' and 'anus' was inserted (idraj) by some narrators. The author first establishes that the overwhelming majority of narrators from Hisham ibn 'Urwah transmitted the hadith without that insertion. He then examines the transmission from Ayyub, where most of his students also narrated without insertion, except for Abu Kamil al-Jahdari who narrated with insertion. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi initially considered Ayyub among those who clarified the inclusion, but later reversed based on Abu Kamil's narration. The author, however, prefers the majority narration from Ayyub. Next, al-Khatib's ruling that 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far was the only one to insert from Hisham is discussed. Al-Hafiz al-'Iraqi objected citing Abu Kamil and Ibn Jurayj, but the author defends al-Khatib by showing both those narrations are weak: Abu Kamil opposed the majority, and Ibn Jurayj's narration was also ruled as inserted by al-Daraqutni and Ibn Hajar. Finally, two additional weak chains from Muhammad ibn Dinar and another are mentioned, confirming the majority position. The overall conclusion is that the authentic version of the hadith does not include the testicles or anus, so the obligation of wudu is limited to touching the penis alone.

Key Terms
الإدراج (al-idrāj): Insertion of extra wording into the text of a hadith by a narrator, not originally part of the Prophet's speech.
الذكر (al-dhakar): The male genital organ (penis).
الأنثيين (al-unthiyayn): The two testicles.
الرفغين (al-rafghayn): The anus or perineum (in this context, likely the anus).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the majority of Ayyub's students narrated from him without idraj.

D) Because Ayyub was a weak narrator.

Key Takeaway
The preponderant version of the wudu hadith excludes the testicles and anus, so the Hanafi ruling is that wudu is not required from touching them.

Identifying Idraj: The Hadith of Touching Private Parts
Textual analysis of hadith chains for idraj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the indicators of idraj (insertion) in a hadith by comparing chains and narrator reliability, and apply this to the hadith of touching private parts.

Core Idea
Isolated additions contradicting the majority are idraj — the authentic hadith of touching private parts does not include 'testicles'.

The hadith of Basrah regarding wudu from touching the private parts is a classic case of idraj (narrator insertion). Some narrators added the word 'al-unthayayn' (the two testicles) to the Prophet's command. This lesson takes you through the chains and scholars' rulings to separate the authentic core from the insertion, a critical skill for anyone studying usul al-fiqh or hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed wording
Locate the textual addition ('al-unthayayn') that some narrators inserted. In the hadith, the original is about touching the penis; the addition extends to the testicles.
This is the key variable in the dispute.
2
Compare the chains for the addition
List the narrators who transmitted the hadith with and without the addition. Note how many narrators from Hisham ibn Urwa and Ayyub included it.
Majority of narrators from Hisham and Ayyub did not include the addition.
3
Evaluate narrator reliability of those who added
Examine the hadith critics' assessments: which narrators are weak, contradicted the majority, or showed memory issues?
For example, Ibn Jurayj's narration was ruled as idraj by al-Daraqutni and Ibn Hajar.
4
Apply the idraj detection principle
The principle: when an addition contradicts what the majority of reliable narrators transmit, it is an insertion (idraj) unless the addition is well-supported.
This is a standard usul al-fiqh tool.
5
Derive the Hanafi position and its fiqh impact
The Hanafi school accepts only the version without the addition, so touching the testicles does not necessitate wudu. The Shafi'i school, relying on the addition, holds that it does.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is in wudu requirements.

والدارقطني. ومحمد بن دينار ليس ممن يعتمد عَلَى حفظه. وروی هشام بن حسان، عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن بسرة مدرجاً. وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عن هشام هكذا مدرجاً اثنان من أصحابه هما: عبد الأعلى بن عبد الأعلى، والدارقطني في العلل قَالَ ابن حجر فتردده يدل على أنه ما ضبطه». وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عمار بن عمر، عن هشام بن حسان من غير إدراج، وروايته أخرجها الطبراني في الكبير والدارقطني في العلل فانتهت نتيجة البحث إلى ضعف المتابع الأول، وعدم ضبط الثاني. وَقَدْ كَانَ لهذا الْحَدِيث أثر فى اختلاف الفقهاء تقدم الكلام عنه في الفصل الثاني المبحث الثالث: ما تعم به البلوى، ولا نريد إعادته بغية عدم الإطالة. ومثال ما وقع الإدراج في آخر الحَدِيث: ما رَوَاهُ زهيـــر بــــن معاوية، عـــــــــن الحــــــن
Chapter Three: Difference in Sanad and Matn. Thus al-Khatib counted Ayyub among those who explained the idraj in the hadith. While Abu Kamil al-Jahdari narrated it from Yazid ibn Zuray', from Ayyub, with idraj, as al-Tabarani recorded, so al-Khatib again counted Ayyub among those who inserted (adraja) the hadith. What is preponderant is the narration of the group from Ayyub, so Ayyub is counted among those who explained idraj. Consequently, the narration of the group who explained idraj in their narration from Hisham ibn Urwa is preponderant. This is supported by the statement of al-Khatib: 'All the companions of Hisham ibn Urwa narrated from him the hadith of wudu from touching the penis specifically, and none of them mentioned the two testicles or the pubic region in his narration.' And al-Khatib al-Baghdadi ruled that Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far was alone in inserting (idraj) from Hisham ibn Urwa. But al-Hafiz al-Iraqi objected with the narration of Abu Kamil al-Jahdari, which was previously discussed, and with the narration of Ibn Jurayj from Hisham ibn Urwa, from his father, from Marwan, from Busrah with the wording: 'If one of you touches his penis or his two testicles.' It appears that al-Khatib's ruling is a restricted ruling, not absolute, and the restriction is mental, because he is unique from an acceptable path. As for these two paths, they are not relied upon for the following: As for Abu Kamil's narration, we have shown that he contradicted the majority of narrators from Ayyub, so it is not considered. As for Ibn Jurayj's narration, al-Daraqutni and al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar ruled it as idraj as well. There are two other paths from Hisham ibn Urwa in which idraj occurred: Muhammad ibn Dinar narrated from Hisham ibn Urwa, from his father, from Busrah this hadith with idraj, and his narration was recorded by al-Tabarani and al-Daraqutni. Muhammad ibn Dinar is not one whose memory is relied upon. And Hisham ibn Hassan narrated from Hisham ibn Urwa, from his father, from Busrah with idraj. Two of his companions narrated from Hisham in this manner with idraj: Abd al-Ala ibn Abd al-Ala, as Ibn Shahin recorded in the book al-Abwab via Ibn Abi Dawud and Yahya ibn Sa'id, both from Muhammad ibn Bashar, from Abd al-Ala, from Ibn Hassan. And al-Daraqutni narrated it in al-Ilal via Abdullah ibn Buzay', from Hisham ibn Hassan. It appears that Hisham ibn Hassan did not memorize the hadith well, because Yazid ibn Harun narrated from him with the wording: 'If one of you touches his penis, or he said his private part, or he said his two testicles, let him perform wudu' – narrated by Ibn Shahin in al-Abwab and al-Daraqutni in al-Ilal. Ibn Hajar said: 'His hesitation indicates he did not memorize it.' Ammar ibn Umar narrated it from Hisham ibn Hassan without idraj, and his narration was recorded by al-Tabarani in al-Kabir and al-Daraqutni in al-Ilal. So the result of the research ended with the weakness of the first follow-up and the lack of precision of the second. This hadith had an impact on the difference among jurists, which was previously discussed in chapter two, section three: 'what is common in need,' and we do not wish to repeat it to avoid elongation. An example of idraj occurring at the end of a hadith: what was narrated by Zuhayr ibn Mu'awiya, from al-Hasan...
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith concerning wudu from touching the private parts, specifically focusing on the issue of idraj (insertion of extra wording into the hadith). The author examines different chains of narration for the hadith of Basrah, which reports the Prophet's command to perform wudu after touching the penis. The dispute revolves around whether the wording 'or his two testicles' is part of the original hadith or an insertion by certain narrators. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi initially identified Ayyub as one who clarified the idraj, but later counted him among those who inserted it. The author weighs the narrations and concludes that the majority of narrators from Ayyub did not include the addition, and that those who did, such as Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far, are isolated in their addition. The objections of al-Iraqi are addressed by showing that the alternative narrations are themselves weak or also contain idraj. The passage then examines other narrators like Muhammad ibn Dinar and Hisham ibn Hassan, who are criticized for lack of precision. Ultimately, the reliable version is the one without the mention of the testicles. This directly affects the Hanafi ruling that only touching the penis, not the testicles or pubic region, breaks wudu. The Hanafi school relies on the version without addition, as supported by this analysis of the chains.

Key Terms
إدراج (idraj): Insertion of extra wording into a hadith by a narrator, not originally part of the Prophet's speech.
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting a hadith.
متن (matn): The text or content of a hadith.
الأنثيين (al-unthayayn): the two testicles

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's analysis, why is the narration of Hisham ibn Hassan considered unreliable?
A) He contradicted the majority of narrators from Ayyub.
B) He showed hesitation in the wording, indicating poor memorization.
C) He narrated from an untrustworthy source.
D) His narration was only found in al-Tabarani's collection.

Key Takeaway
The authentic hadith of wudu from touching only mentions the penis; the addition of 'testicles' is an idraj rejected by the majority of reliable narrators.

Idraj in the Hadith on Touching Private Parts
Example of idraj in a hadith on wudu after touching private parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the signs of idraj in a hadith text using the example of the private parts hadith.

Core Idea
A narrator's insertion can change a ruling; idraj must be detected by comparing chains and wordings.

This lesson examines how a hadith on touching private parts was affected by idraj. The narrator Hisham bin Hassan's lack of precision led to varying wordings, including an insertion from his own interpretation. Understanding this process is essential for evaluating hadith evidence in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator and his weakness
Hisham bin Hassan is noted as not fully precise; his memory is questioned.
Weakness in a narrator raises suspicion about additions.
2
Note the variations in wording
The hadith includes 'penis,' 'private part,' and 'testicles' in different transmissions.
Hesitation in wording indicates possible insertion.
3
Compare narrations with and without the insertion
Ammar bin Umar narrated without the testicles addition, suggesting that addition is not original.
Multiple chains help isolate the insertion.
4
Conclude the addition is mudraj
Scholars conclude that Hisham's variations show he did not memorize well; the testicles phrase is from his own words.
Idraj invalidates the addition as prophetic evidence.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
و محمد بن دينار ليس ممن يعتمد عَلَى حفظه. وروی هشام بن حسان، عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن بسرة مدرجاً. وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عن هشام هكذا مدرجاً اثنان من أصحابه هما: عبد الأعلى بن عبد الأعلى، حَيْثُ رَوَاهُ ابن شاهين في كتاب " الأبواب " من طريق ابن أبي داود ويحيى بن صاعد كلاهما عن مُحَمَّد بن بشار، عن عبد الأعلى، - عن ابن حسان.
ورواه الدارقطني في " العلل من طريق عَبْد الله بن بزيع، عن هشام بن حسان به.
والظاهر أن هشام بن حسان لَمْ يضبط الْحَدِيْث جيداً، إِذْ رَوَاهُ يزيد بن هارون عَنْهُ بلفظ: «إذا مس أحدكم ذكره أو قَالَ فرجه، أو قَالَ: أنثييه، فليتوضأ» رَوَاهُ ابن شاهين في كتاب " الأبواب "، والدارقطني في " العلل ". قَالَ ابن حجر فتردده يدل على أنه ما ضبطه.
وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عمار بن عمر، عن هشام بن حسان من غير إدراج، وروايته أخرجها الطبراني في " الكبير "، والدارقطني في " العلل ". فانتهت نتيجة البحث إلى ضعف المتابع الأول، وعدم ضبط الثاني. وَقَدْ كَانَ لهذا الْحَدِيث أثر فى اختلاف الفقهاء تقدم الكلام عنه في الفصل الثاني المبحث الثالث: ما تعم به البلوى، ولا نريد إعادته بغية عدم الإطالة.
ومثال ما وقع الإدراج في آخر الحَدِيث: ما رَوَاهُ زهير بن معاوية، عَنِ الْحَسَنِ بْنِ الْحُرِّ، عَنِ الْقَاسِمِ بْنِ مُخَيْمِرَةَ، عَنْ عَلْقَمَةَ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلَّمَهُ التَّشَهُّدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، فَقَالَ: «قُلِ: التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ... فَذَكَرَ الْحَدِيثَ». وَفِي آخِرِهِ: «أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ، فَإِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَضَيْتَ صَلَاتَكَ إِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ، وَإِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدْ». فَزِيَادَةُ: «فَإِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا ... إِلَى نِهَايَةِ الرِّوَايَةِ مُدْرَجَةٌ مِنْ قَوْلِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، أَدْرَجَهَا زُهَيْرُ بْنُ مُعَاوِيَةَ فِي رِوَايَتِهِ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ بْنِ الْحُرِّ، نَصَّ عَلَى هَذَا الْحُفَّاظُ مِنْهُمْ: الدَّارَقُطْنِي، وَالْحَاكِمُ، وَالْبَيْهَقِيُّ، وَالْخَطِيبُ الْبَغْدَادِيُّ، وَنُقِلَ عَنِ النَّوَوِيِّ فِي " الْخُلَاصَةِ " اتِّفَاقُ الْحُفَّاظِ عَلَى إِدْرَاجِهَا.
وَاسْتَدَلَّ الْحَافِظُ ابْنُ الصَّلَاحِ عَلَى الْإِدْرَاجِ بِقَوْلِهِ: (وَمِنَ الدَّلِيلِ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ الثِّقَةَ الزَّاهِدَ عَبْدَ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنَ ثَابِتِ بْنِ ثَوْبَانَ، رَوَاهُ عَنْ رَاوِيهِ الْحَسَنِ بْنِ الْحُرِّ كَذَلِكَ، وَاتَّفَقَ).
Chapter Three / Disagreement in Chain and Text. And Muhammad bin Dinar is not one whose memory is relied upon. And Hisham bin Hassan narrated from Hisham bin Urwa from his father from Busra as an insertion (mudraj). And it was narrated from Hisham in this inserted form by two of his companions: Abd al-A'la bin Abd al-A'la, where Ibn Shahin narrated it in the book "al-Abwab" via Ibn Abi Dawud and Yahya bin Sa'id both from Muhammad bin Bashshar from Abd al-A'la from Ibn Hassan. And al-Daraqutni narrated it in "al-'Ilal" via Abdullah bin Buzay' from Hisham bin Hassan with it. And it appears that Hisham bin Hassan did not memorize the hadith well, since Yazid bin Harun narrated it from him with the wording: "If one of you touches his penis, or he said his private part, or he said his testicles, let him perform ablution." Ibn Shahin narrated it in "al-Abwab" and al-Daraqutni in "al-'Ilal". Ibn Hajar said: his hesitation indicates that he did not memorize it. And Ammar bin Umar narrated it from Hisham bin Hassan without insertion, and his narration was narrated by al-Tabarani in "al-Kabir" and al-Daraqutni in "al-'Ilal". The conclusion of the research was the weakness of the first follow-up and the lack of precision of the second. And this hadith had an impact on the disagreement of jurists, which was discussed earlier in Chapter Two, Section Three: on matters of general affliction; we do not wish to repeat it to avoid length. And an example of insertion occurring at the end of the hadith: what Zuhayr bin Mu'awiya narrated from al-Hasan bin al-Hurr from al-Qasim bin Mukhaymira from Alqama from Abdullah bin Mas'ud that the Messenger of Allah taught him the tashahhud in prayer, saying: "Say: 'Greetings to Allah...' and he mentioned the hadith." And at its end: "I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. When you have said this, you have completed your prayer; if you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit." The addition "When you have said this... to the end of the narration" is inserted (mudraj) from the statement of Ibn Mas'ud; Zuhayr bin Mu'awiya inserted it into his narration from al-Hasan bin al-Hurr. This was stated by the hadith scholars including: al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, and it was reported from al-Nawawi in "al-Khulasa" that the scholars agreed upon its insertion. And Ibn al-Salah argued for the insertion by saying: "Evidence for it is that the trustworthy ascetic Abd al-Rahman bin Thabit bin Thuban narrated it from his narrator al-Hasan bin al-Hurr in the same way, and they agreed."
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is from the third chapter on disagreement in chain and text, focusing on the phenomenon of idraj (insertion) in hadith. The author provides two examples to illustrate how idraj affects fiqh differences. First, the hadith about touching the private parts: the narrator Hisham bin Hassan is criticized for lack of precision; his wording fluctuates, indicating weak memory. Some narrators added the part about testicles, which led to juristic disagreement on whether touching the private parts invalidates wudu. The author notes that this was covered earlier. Second, the tashahhud hadith: the addition at the end permitting sitting or standing after testifying was inserted by Zuhayr bin Mu'awiya from the statement of Ibn Mas'ud, not from the Prophet. Scholars like al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirmed the idraj. Ibn al-Salah provides evidence that another narrator transmitted without the addition. Understanding idraj is crucial for Hanafi usul al-fiqh because it affects the authenticity of evidence used in deriving rulings.

Key Terms
إدراج (idraj): Insertion of a narrator's own statement into the hadith text, making it appear as part of the prophetic wording
مدرج (mudraj): A hadith with an insertion; the added part is from a narrator, not the Prophet

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did scholars consider the addition of 'testicles' in the hadith about touching private parts to be mudraj?
A) Because the narrator Hisham bin Hassan was known to be a liar
B) Because Hisham's wording varied and another reliable narration omitted the testicles phrase
C) Because the addition contradicts the Quran
D) Because the addition is about wudu, not about touching

Key Takeaway
Idraj can change a ruling; detection requires careful comparison of chains and wordings.
