Five Causes of Idraj in Hadith
Listing causes of idraj with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each cause of idraj and apply the Hanafi methodology for detecting inserted material in hadith.

Core Idea
Idraj: when a narrator's explanation becomes part of the hadith, requiring careful scrutiny.

Hadith are the second source of Islamic law, but not every word attributed to the Prophet ﷺ is authentic. One subtle defect is idraj, where a narrator's own words become mixed into the hadith text. This lesson explores the five causes of idraj as outlined in classical usul works, equipping you to recognize such insertions and preserve the integrity of prophetic traditions.

Guided Path
1
Define idraj and its significance
Idraj is the insertion of non-prophetic words into a hadith, affecting its authenticity. Recognize that idraj can be unintentional and is not the same as outright fabrication.
2
Examine each of the five causes
The text lists: explanation of unfamiliar words, proving a ruling, deriving a ruling, abbreviation/narration by meaning, and lack of precision. Study the examples given for each.
3
Analyze the mechanism of insertion
In each cause, understand how the narrator's own speech became mixed with the prophetic text. Note the role of subsequent transmitters.
4
Evaluate the impact on fiqh rulings
Consider how mudraj hadith can lead to incorrect rulings if not identified. Hanafi scholars scrutinize such hadith by comparing narrations and checking for inserted phrases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثالث
أسباب وقوع الإدراج
إن الباعث للراوي على الإدراج يختلف من شخص لآخر، ومن حَدِيث إلى حَدِيث غيره، ما بَيْنَ بيان لتفسير كلمة، أو استنباط لحكم، أو قلة ضبط.
ويمكننا أن نجمل سبب وقوع الإدراج فيما يأتي(۳): 1. أن يريد الرَّاوِي تفسير بعض الألفاظ الغريبة الواردة في متن الْحَدِيث، فيحملها عَنْهُ بعض الرُّوَاة من غَيْر تفصيل لتفسير تِلْكَ الألفاظ.
مثاله : حَدِيث عقيل (4) ، عن ابن شهاب الزهري، عن عروة بن الزبير، عن عائشة أم المؤمنين في قصة بدء الوحي، وفيه: «وَكان يخلو بغار حراء فيتحنث فِيهِ، وَهُوَ التعبد ...»( ).
فقوله: «وَهُوَ التعبد» مدرج من كلام الزهري في الْحَدِيث).
۲ أن يقصد الرَّاوِي إثبات حكم ويستدل عليه بالحديث المرفوع. ومثاله ما سبق (۱) في حَدِيث أَبِي هُرَيْرَة : أسبغوا الوضوء، ويل للأعقاب من النار.
۳ أن يريد الرَّاوِي بيان حكم يُستنبط من كلام النَّبِي . ومثاله ما تقدم) في حَدِيث بسرة بنت صفوان رضي الله عَنْهَا: «مَنْ مس ذكره أو رفعه أو أنثييه فليتوضأ». قَالَ السيوطي: «فعروة لمّا فهم من لفظ الخبر أن سبب نقض الوضوء مظنة الشهوة جعل حكم ما قرب من الذكر كذلك فَقَالَ ذَلِكَ، فظن بعض الرُّوَاة أنه من صلب الخبر فنقله مدرجاً فيه، وفهم الآخرون الحال فصلوا (۳).
٤. اختصار الْحَدِيث والرواية بالمعنى.
ه الخطأ الناشئ عن عدم ضبط الرَّاوِي لمروياته.
Third Section: Causes of Occurrence of Idraj. The motivation for the narrator to insert varies from person to person and from hadith to hadith, whether for explanation of a word, derivation of a ruling, or lack of precision. We can summarize the cause of idraj as follows: 1. The narrator wants to explain some unfamiliar words in the hadith text, so some narrators transmit it from him without distinguishing the explanation of those words. Example: Hadith of 'Uqayl from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri from 'Urwa ibn al-Zubayr from 'A'isha in the story of the beginning of revelation, in which it says: 'He used to seclude himself in the cave of Hira and tahannuth therein, which means worship.' His saying 'which means worship' is inserted from the speech of al-Zuhri into the hadith. 2. The narrator intends to prove a ruling and uses the marfu' hadith as evidence. Example: The hadith of Abu Hurayra: 'Perform wudu thoroughly; woe to the heels from the Fire.' 3. The narrator wants to explain a ruling derived from the words of the Prophet. Example: The hadith of Busra bint Safwan: 'Whoever touches his penis, or his scrotum, or his testicles, let him perform wudu.' Al-Suyuti said: 'When 'Urwa understood from the wording of the hadith that the cause of breaking wudu is the likelihood of desire, he regarded the ruling of what is near the penis as similar, so he said that. Then some narrators thought it was part of the hadith and transmitted it inserted, while others understood the situation and separated.' 4. Abbreviation of the hadith and narration by meaning. 5. The error arising from the narrator's lack of control over his narrations.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage categorizes the reasons why idraj occurs, providing concrete examples from hadith. The first cause is when a narrator explains unfamiliar terms without clarifying that the explanation is his own, leading to its insertion. Example: In the hadith of revelation, the word 'tahannuth' was explained as 'worship' by al-Zuhri; this explanation became inserted. The second cause is when a narrator intends to support a ruling with a hadith but inserts his own conclusion. Example: The hadith about wiping heels is reported, but the phrase 'Aghislu al-wudu' might be inserted. The third cause is similar but from the narrator's derivation. Example: The hadith about touching the penis; 'Urwa added the scrotum and testicles based on his understanding, which was inserted by some. The fourth cause is abbreviation and narration by meaning, which can lead to insertion of explanatory remarks. The fifth cause is simple error due to lack of precision. In Hanafi fiqh, these examples are used to illustrate how hadith can become mudraj and how careful scrutiny is needed.

Key Terms
الإدراج (al-idraj): Insertion of extraneous material into a hadith
المدرج (al-mudraj): A hadith containing such insertion
الرواية بالمعنى (al-riwayah bi al-ma'na): Narrating the meaning of a hadith rather than its exact wording

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a cause of idraj?
A) Explaining unfamiliar words.
B) Deriving a ruling from the Prophet's words.
C) Deliberate fabrication of hadith.
D) Abbreviation and narration by meaning.

Key Takeaway
Idraj is a serious issue in hadith methodology; its detection requires careful analysis of narrations and awareness of common causes.
